         </a>
         density
        </th>
        <td>

         <sup>

         </sup>
         (859/sq mi)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr class="mergedtoprow">

       <tr class="mergedtoprow">
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">

         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_408" title="Area code 408">
          408
         </a>
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Area_codes_408_and_669" title="Area codes 408 and 669">
          669
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_415" title="Area code 415">
          415
         </a>
         /
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_628" title="Area code 628">
          628
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_510" title="Area code 510">
          510
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_650" title="Area code 650">
          650
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_707" title="Area code 707">
          707
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_925" title="Area code 925">

         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
          <a href="#cite_note-6">
           [6]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        San Francisco Bay Area
       </b>
       (referred to locally as the
       <b>
        Bay Area
       </b>
       ) is a populous region surrounding the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Bay" title="San Pablo Bay">
        San Pablo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Suisun_Bay" title="Suisun Bay">
        Suisun
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuaries
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        U.S.
       </a>
       state of
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       . Although the exact boundaries of the region vary depending on the source, the Bay Area is generally accepted to include the nine counties that border the aforementioned estuaries:
       <a href="/wiki/Alameda_County,_California" title="Alameda County, California">
        Alameda
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Contra_Costa_County,_California" title="Contra Costa County, California">
        Contra Costa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
        Marin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Napa_County,_California" title="Napa County, California">
        Napa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo_County,_California" title="San Mateo County, California">
        San Mateo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">
        Santa Clara
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Solano_County,_California" title="Solano County, California">
        Solano
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_County,_California" title="Sonoma County, California">
        Sonoma
       </a>
       . Other sources may exclude parts of or even entire counties, or include neighboring counties such as
       <a href="/wiki/San_Benito_County,_California" title="San Benito County, California">
        San Benito
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_County,_California" title="San Joaquin County, California">
        San Joaquin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_County,_California" title="Santa Cruz County, California">
        Santa Cruz
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Home to approximately 7.68 million people, the nine-county Bay Area contains many cities, towns, airports, and associated regional, state, and
       <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">
        national parks
       </a>
       , connected by a complex multimodal transportation network. The larger
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Jose-San_Francisco-Oakland,_CA_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="San Jose-San Francisco-Oakland, CA Combined Statistical Area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       of the region, which includes twelve counties, is the second-largest in
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       (after the
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">
        Greater Los Angeles
       </a>
       area), the fifth-largest in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_by_population" title="List of urban areas by population">
        41st-largest urban area in the world
       </a>
       with 8.75 million people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bay Area's population is ethnically diverse: for example, roughly half of the region's residents are
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanic
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
        Asian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">
        African American
       </a>
       , or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">
        Pacific Islander
       </a>
       , all of whom have a significant presence throughout the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       The earliest archaeological evidence of human settlements in the Bay Area dates back to 3000 BC. In 1769, the Bay Area was inhabited by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ohlone" title="Ohlone">
        Ohlone
       </a>
       people when a
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish exploration party
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_de_Portol%C3%A0" title="Gaspar de Portolà">
        Gaspar de Portolà
       </a>
       entered the Bay – the first documented European visit to the Bay Area. After
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">
        established independence
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       in 1821, the region was briefly controlled by the Mexican government until the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       seized the territory in 1846 during the
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">
        Mexican–American War
       </a>
       . Soon after,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_gold_rush" title="California gold rush">
        discovery of gold
       </a>
       in California attracted a flood of treasure seekers, many using ports in the Bay Area as an entry point. During the early years of California's statehood, state legislative business rotated between three locations in the Bay Area before a permanent state capital was established in
       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">
        Sacramento
       </a>
       . A
       <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">
        major earthquake
       </a>
       leveled the city of San Francisco and environs in 1906, but the region quickly rebuilt in time to host the
       <a href="/wiki/Panama%E2%80%93Pacific_International_Exposition" title="Panama–Pacific International Exposition">
        1915 Panama-Pacific Exposition
       </a>
       . During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the Bay Area played a major role in America's war effort in the
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatic-Pacific_Theater" title="Asiatic-Pacific Theater">
        Asiatic-Pacific Theater
       </a>
       , with San Francisco's
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mason" title="Fort Mason">
        Fort Mason
       </a>
       acting as a primary embarkation point for American forces. In 1945, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">
        United Nations Charter
       </a>
       was signed in San Francisco, establishing the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       , and in 1951, the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">
        Treaty of San Francisco
       </a>
       officially ended the U.S.'s
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">
        war with Japan
       </a>
       . Since then, the Bay Area has experienced numerous political, cultural and artistic movements, developing unique local genres in music and art and establishing itself as a hotbed of
       <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">
        progressive politics
       </a>
       . Economically, the post-war Bay Area saw huge growth in the financial and technology industries, creating a vibrant and diverse economy with a
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        gross domestic product
       </a>
       of over $700 billion, and home to the second highest concentration of
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       companies in the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite its urban character, the San Francisco Bay is one of California's most ecologically important habitats, providing key ecosystem services such as filtering pollutants and sediments from the rivers, and supporting a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">
        endangered species
       </a>
       . The region is also known for the complexity of its landforms, the result of millions of years of
       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">
        tectonic plate
       </a>
       movements. Because the Bay Area is crossed by six major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earthquake_fault" title="Earthquake fault">
        earthquake faults
       </a>
       , the region is particularly exposed to hazards presented by large earthquakes. The climate is temperate and generally very mild, and is ideal for outdoor recreational and athletic activities such as hiking. The Bay Area is host to seven
       <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">
        professional sports
       </a>
       teams and is a cultural center for music, theater, and the arts. It is also host to several institutions of higher education, ranging from
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">
        primary schools
       </a>
       to major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_universities" title="Research universities">
        research universities
       </a>
       . Home to 101 municipalities and nine counties, governance in the Bay Area is multifaceted and involves numerous local and regional actors, each with wide-ranging and overlapping responsibilities.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boundaries">
        Boundaries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Boundaries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayarea_map.png">
         <img alt="A map demarcating the boundaries of the nine-county Bay Area and the five subregions within." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1732" data-file-width="1539" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayarea_map.png/220px-Bayarea_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayarea_map.png/330px-Bayarea_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bayarea_map.png/440px-Bayarea_map.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayarea_map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of the locally accepted nine-county definition of the Bay Area. Also displayed are the five subregions of the Bay Area, which are divided along county lines except for the northwestern portion of
         <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">
          Santa Clara county
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The borders of the San Francisco Bay Area are not officially delineated, and the unique development patterns influenced by the region's topography, along with the presence of unusual commute patterns caused by the presence of three central cities and employment centers located in suburban cities, has led to considerable disagreement between local and federal definitions of the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-walker-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of this, professor of
       <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">
        geography
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">
        University of California, Berkeley
       </a>
       Richard Walker claimed that "no other U.S. city-region is as definitionally challenged [as the Bay Area]."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-walker-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Locally, many of the regional governmental agencies and districts recognize the nine counties that border the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Bay" title="San Pablo Bay">
        San Pablo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Suisun_Bay" title="Suisun Bay">
        Suisun
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuaries
       </a>
       as part of the Bay Area:
       <a href="/wiki/Alameda_County,_California" title="Alameda County, California">
        Alameda
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Contra_Costa_County,_California" title="Contra Costa County, California">
        Contra Costa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
        Marin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Napa_County,_California" title="Napa County, California">
        Napa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo_County,_California" title="San Mateo County, California">
        San Mateo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">
        Santa Clara
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Solano_County,_California" title="Solano County, California">
        Solano
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_County,_California" title="Sonoma County, California">
        Sonoma
       </a>
       counties. These agencies include the
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Water_Resources_Control_Board#Regional_Water_Quality_Control_Boards" title="California State Water Resources Control Board">
        San Francisco Regional Water Quality Control Board
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Air_Quality_Management_District" title="Bay Area Air Quality Management District">
        Bay Area Air Quality Management District
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutbaaqmd_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aboutbaaqmd-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Restoration_Authority" title="San Francisco Bay Restoration Authority">
        San Francisco Bay Restoration Authority
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transportation_Commission_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="Metropolitan Transportation Commission (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        Metropolitan Transportation Commission
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Bay_Area_Governments" title="Association of Bay Area Governments">
        Association of Bay Area Governments
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the latter two of which partner to deliver a Bay Area Census using the nine-county definition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Various
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Federal_Government" title="United States Federal Government">
        U.S. Federal government
       </a>
       agencies use definitions that differ from their local counterparts' nine-county definition. For example, the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">
        Federal Communications Commission
       </a>
       (FCC) which regulates broadcast, cable, and satellite transmissions, includes nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Colusa_County,_California" title="Colusa County, California">
        Colusa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_California" title="Lake County, California">
        Lake
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mendocino_County,_California" title="Mendocino County, California">
        Mendocino
       </a>
       counties in their "San Francisco-Oakland-San Jose"
       <a href="/wiki/Media_market#United_States" title="Media market">
        media market
       </a>
       , but excludes eastern Solano county.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the other hand, the United States
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
        Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       , which designates
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        Metropolitan Statistical Areas
       </a>
       (MSAs) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">
        Combined Statistical Areas
       </a>
       (CSA) for populated regions across the country, has five MSAs which include, wholly or partially, areas within the nine-county definition, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Jose-San_Francisco-Oakland,_CA_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="San Jose-San Francisco-Oakland, CA Combined Statistical Area">
        one CSA which includes
       </a>
       all nine counties plus neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/San_Benito_County,_California" title="San Benito County, California">
        San Benito
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_County,_California" title="Santa Cruz County, California">
        Santa Cruz
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_County,_California" title="San Joaquin County, California">
        San Joaquin
       </a>
       counties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMB_13-01_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OMB_13-01-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Subregions">
        Subregions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Subregions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Among locals, the nine-county Bay Area can be further divided into five sub-regions: the
       <a href="/wiki/East_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="East Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        East Bay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="North Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        North Bay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_Valley" title="Santa Clara Valley">
        South Bay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Peninsula" title="San Francisco Peninsula">
        Peninsula
       </a>
       , and the city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" title="San Francisco, California">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       . Although geographically located on the tip of the San Francisco Peninsula, the city of San Francisco is not considered part of the "Peninsula" subregion, but as a separate entity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crawford2006_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Crawford2006-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The "
       <a href="/wiki/East_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="East Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        East Bay
       </a>
       " is the densest region of the Bay Area outside of San Francisco and includes cities and towns in Alameda and Contra Costa counties, centered around
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       . As one of the larger subregions, the East Bay includes a variety of enclaves, including the suburban
       <a href="/wiki/Tri-Valley" title="Tri-Valley">
        Tri-Valley
       </a>
       area and the highly urban western part of the subregion that runs alongside the bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The "
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Peninsula" title="San Francisco Peninsula">
        Peninsula
       </a>
       " subregion includes the cities and towns on the San Francisco Peninsula, excluding the titular city of San Francisco. Its eastern half, which runs alongside the Bay, is highly populated while its less populated western coast traces the coastline of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       and is known for its open space and hiking trails. Roughly coinciding with the borders of San Mateo county, it also includes the northwestern Santa Clara county cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">
        Palo Alto
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">
        Mountain View
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos,_California" title="Los Altos, California">
        Los Altos
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The "South Bay" includes all of the rest of the cities in Santa Clara county, centered around
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
        San Jose
       </a>
       , and is roughly synonymous with
       <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">
        Silicon Valley
       </a>
       due to its high concentration of tech companies, although the industry also has a significant presence in the rest of the Bay Area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The "
       <a href="/wiki/North_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="North Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        North Bay
       </a>
       " includes Marin, Sonoma, Napa, and Solano counties, and is the largest and least populated subregion. The western counties of Marin and Sonoma are encased by the Pacific Ocean on the west and the bay on the east, and are characterized by its mountainous and woody terrain. Sonoma and Napa counties are known internationally for their grape vineyards and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wineries" title="Wineries">
        wineries
       </a>
       , and Solano county to the east, centered around
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       , is the fastest growing region in the Bay Area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Timeline of the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Timeline of the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg">
         <img alt="A sketch of the native Ohlone people performing a dance." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg/220px-Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg/330px-Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg/440px-Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mission_San_Jose_natives.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An early sketch of the
         <a href="/wiki/Ohlone" title="Ohlone">
          Ohlone
         </a>
         people dancing in
         <a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Jos%C3%A9_(California)" title="Mission San José (California)">
          Mission San Jose
         </a>
         . The Ohlone lived in the Bay Area when European colonizers first arrived in the region.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric_migration_and_settlement_of_the_Americas_from_Asia" title="Prehistoric migration and settlement of the Americas from Asia">
        settlement of the Americas
       </a>
       occurred some 20,000 years ago, when the first Asians crossed the
       <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">
        Bering Strait
       </a>
       into
       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
        Alaska
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohlone1_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ohlone1-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the earliest archaeological evidence of human habitation of the Bay Area dates to around 3,000
       <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">
        B.C.
       </a>
       along the shores of the bay, with evidence pointing to even earlier settlement in
       <a href="/wiki/Point_Reyes" title="Point Reyes">
        Point Reyes
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
        Marin County
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Miwok" title="Miwok">
        Miwokan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ohlone" title="Ohlone">
        Costanoan Ohlone
       </a>
       people, who were living in the Bay Area at the time of first European contact, were possibly descended from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian" title="Siberian">
        Siberian
       </a>
       tribes who arrived at around 1,000 BC by sailing over the
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">
        Arctic Ocean
       </a>
       and following the salmon migration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohlone1_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ohlone1-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ohlone lived in about forty or so tribes spread throughout the lands adjacent to the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco Bay
       </a>
       and as far south as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Point_Sur" title="Point Sur">
        Point Sur
       </a>
       in near
       <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Bay" title="Monterey Bay">
        Monterey Bay
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SanFrancisco1851a.jpg">
         <img alt="An old image of Portsmouth Square from 1851." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1581" data-file-width="3252" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SanFrancisco1851a.jpg/220px-SanFrancisco1851a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SanFrancisco1851a.jpg/330px-SanFrancisco1851a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/SanFrancisco1851a.jpg/440px-SanFrancisco1851a.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SanFrancisco1851a.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Bay Area was briefly controlled by
         <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
          Mexico
         </a>
         until
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Berrien_Montgomery" title="John Berrien Montgomery">
          John Berrien Montgomery
         </a>
         captured San Francisco during the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" title="Mexican-American War">
          Mexican-American War
         </a>
         and raised the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_flag" title="American flag">
          American flag
         </a>
         over
         <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Square" title="Portsmouth Square">
          Portsmouth Square
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1575, a
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish exploration party
       </a>
       led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebastian_Rodriguez_Cermeno" title="Sebastian Rodriguez Cermeno">
        Sebastian Rodriguez Cermeno
       </a>
       landed in
       <a href="/wiki/Drakes_Bay" title="Drakes Bay">
        Drakes Bay
       </a>
       near Point Reyes and was the first European settler to claim land in the Bay Area. He was soon followed in 1579 by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Francis_Drake" title="Sir Francis Drake">
        Sir Francis Drake
       </a>
       , who also landed in Drakes Bay and claimed the land for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="English colonization of the Americas">
        England
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The San Francisco Bay itself remained undiscovered by Europeans until a Spanish expedition led by
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_de_Portol%C3%A0" title="Gaspar de Portolà">
        Gaspar de Portolà
       </a>
       sailed through the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Strait" title="Golden Gate Strait">
        Golden Gate Strait
       </a>
       in 1769.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_25-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Further expeditions by Spanish explorers in the following years include those led by
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bautista_de_Anza" title="Juan Bautista de Anza">
        Juan Bautista de Anza
       </a>
       who colonized the
       <a href="/wiki/Presidio" title="Presidio">
        Presidio
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Moraga" title="Gabriel Moraga">
        Gabriel Moraga
       </a>
       who started at the Presidio and led expedition parties to
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
        San Jose
       </a>
       and over the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacheco_Pass" title="Pacheco Pass">
        Pacheco Pass
       </a>
       , as well as reaching the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">
        San Joaquin Valley
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_25-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1821,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">
        gained its independence
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and the Bay Area became part of the Mexican province of
       <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">
        Alta California
       </a>
       , a period characterized by
       <a href="/wiki/Ranchos_of_California" title="Ranchos of California">
        ranch life
       </a>
       and visiting
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        American
       </a>
       trappers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nps_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nps-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mexico's control of the territory would be short-lived, however, and in 1846, a party of settlers
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt" title="Bear Flag Revolt">
        occupied
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_Plaza" title="Sonoma Plaza">
        Sonoma Plaza
       </a>
       and proclaimed the independence of the new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_California" title="Republic of California">
        Republic of California
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nps_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nps-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That same year, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" title="Mexican-American War">
        Mexican-American War
       </a>
       began, and American captain
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Berrien_Montgomery" title="John Berrien Montgomery">
        John Berrien Montgomery
       </a>
       sailed the
       <a href="/wiki/USS_Portsmouth_(1843)" title="USS Portsmouth (1843)">
        USS
        <i>
         Portsmouth
        </i>
       </a>
       into the bay and seized San Francisco, which was then known as
       <a href="/wiki/Yerba_Buena,_California" title="Yerba Buena, California">
        Yerba Buena
       </a>
       , and raised the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_flag" title="American flag">
        American flag
       </a>
       for the first time over
       <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Square" title="Portsmouth Square">
        Portsmouth Square
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sutters_Mill.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of Sutter's Mill, where the Gold Rush took place." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1291" data-file-width="1614" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sutters_Mill.jpg/220px-Sutters_Mill.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sutters_Mill.jpg/330px-Sutters_Mill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Sutters_Mill.jpg/440px-Sutters_Mill.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sutters_Mill.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">
          Discovery of gold
         </a>
         near
         <a href="/wiki/Sutter%27s_Mill" title="Sutter's Mill">
          Sutter's Mill
         </a>
         transformed the Bay Area, which saw a flood of immigrants seeking wealth and hoping to strike it rich.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1848,
       <a href="/wiki/James_W._Marshall" title="James W. Marshall">
        James W. Marshall
       </a>
       's discovery of gold in the
       <a href="/wiki/American_River" title="American River">
        American River
       </a>
       sparked the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">
        California Gold Rush
       </a>
       , and within half a year, 4,000 men were panning for gold along the river and finding $50,000 per day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richardson_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Richardson-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The promise of fabulous riches quickly led to a stampede of wealth-seekers descending on
       <a href="/wiki/Sutter%27s_Mill" title="Sutter's Mill">
        Sutter's Mill
       </a>
       . The Bay Area's population quickly emptied out as laborers, clerks, waiters, and servants joined the rush to find gold, and California's first newspaper,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Californian_(1840s_newspaper)" title="The Californian (1840s newspaper)">
         The Californian
        </a>
       </i>
       , was forced to announce a temporary freeze in new issues due to labor shortages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richardson_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Richardson-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the end of 1849, news had spread across the world and newcomers flooded into the Bay Area at a rate of one thousand per week on their way to California's interior,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richardson_29-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Richardson-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including the first large influx of Chinese immigrants to the U.S.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rush was so great that vessels were abandoned by the hundreds in San Francisco's ports as crews rushed to the gold fields.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buriedships_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-buriedships-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The unprecedented influx of new arrivals spread the nascent government authorities thin, and the military was unable to prevent desertions. As a result, numerous vigilante groups formed to provide order, but many tasked themselves with forcibly moving or killing local
       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
        Native Americans
       </a>
       , and by the end of the Gold Rush, two thirds of the indigenous population had been killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During this same time, a
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_(California)" title="Constitutional Convention (California)">
        constitutional convention
       </a>
       was called to determine California's application for
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_admission_to_the_Union" title="List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union">
        statehood
       </a>
       into the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       . After statehood was granted, the capital city moved between three cities in the Bay Area: San Jose (1849–1851),
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       (1851–1852), and
       <a href="/wiki/Benicia,_California" title="Benicia, California">
        Benicia
       </a>
       (1852–1853) before permanently settling in
       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">
        Sacramento
       </a>
       in 1854.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the Gold Rush wound down, wealth generated from the endeavor led to the establishment of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Bank" title="Wells Fargo Bank">
        Wells Fargo Bank
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_California" title="Bank of California">
        Bank of California
       </a>
       , and immigrant laborers attracted by the promise of wealth transformed the demographic makeup of the region. Construction of the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Transcontinental_Railroad" title="First Transcontinental Railroad">
        First Transcontinental Railroad
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Long_Wharf" title="Oakland Long Wharf">
        Oakland Long Wharf
       </a>
       attracted so many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Railroad_Workers" title="Chinese Railroad Workers">
        laborers from China
       </a>
       that by 1870, eight percent of San Francisco's population was of Asian origin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The completion of the railroad connected the Bay Area with the rest of the United States, established a truly national marketplace for the trade of goods, and accelerated the urbanization of the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg">
         <img alt="A historical image of damaged and destroyed buildings after the 1906 earthquake in San Francisco" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1764" data-file-width="2369" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg/220px-Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg/330px-Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg/440px-Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Post-and-Grant-Avenue-Look.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Damaged buildings in the aftermath of the
         <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">
          1906 San Francisco earthquake
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early morning of April 18, 1906,
       <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">
        a large earthquake
       </a>
       with an epicenter near the city of San Francisco hit the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Immediate casualty estimates by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army" title="U.S. Army">
        U.S. Army
       </a>
       's relief operations were 498 deaths in San Francisco, 64 deaths in
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa,_California" title="Santa Rosa, California">
        Santa Rosa
       </a>
       , and 102 in or near San Jose, for a total of about 700. More recent studies estimate the total death count to be over 3,000, with over 28,000 buildings destroyed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rebuilding efforts began immediately.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amadeo_Peter_Giannini" title="Amadeo Peter Giannini">
        Amadeo Peter Giannini
       </a>
       , owner of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_of_Italy_(USA)" title="Bank of Italy (USA)">
        Bank of Italy
       </a>
       (now known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">
        Bank of America
       </a>
       ), had managed to retrieve the money from his bank's vaults before fires broke out through the city and was the only bank with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquidity" title="Liquidity">
        liquid
       </a>
       funds readily available and was instrumental in loaning out funds for rebuilding efforts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthquakeaftermath_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-earthquakeaftermath-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Congress immediately approved plans for a reservoir in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hetch_Hetchy_Valley" title="Hetch Hetchy Valley">
        Hetch Hetchy Valley
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Yosemite_National_Park" title="Yosemite National Park">
        Yosemite National Park
       </a>
       , a plan they had denied a few years earlier, which now provides drinking water for 2.4 million people in the Bay Area. By 1915, the city had been sufficiently rebuilt and advertised itself to the world during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panama_Pacific_Exposition" title="Panama Pacific Exposition">
        Panama Pacific Exposition
       </a>
       that year, although the effects of the quake hastened the loss of the region's dominant status in California to the
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">
        Los Angeles metropolitan area
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthquakeaftermath_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-earthquakeaftermath-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UnitedNationsconference.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of President Truman speaking at a podium, addressing the United Nations Convention." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="216" data-file-width="300" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/UnitedNationsconference.jpg/220px-UnitedNationsconference.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/UnitedNationsconference.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UnitedNationsconference.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         U.S. President
         <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">
          Harry S. Truman
         </a>
         addressing the
         <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization" title="United Nations Conference on International Organization">
          United Nations Conference
         </a>
         in San Francisco that established the
         <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
          United Nations
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">
        1929 stock market crash
       </a>
       and subsequent
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        economic depression
       </a>
       , not a single San Francisco-based bank failed,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while the region attempted to spur job growth by simultaneously undertaking two large infrastructure projects: construction of the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">
        Golden Gate Bridge
       </a>
       , which would connect San Francisco with
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
        Marin County
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco-Oakland_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco-Oakland Bay Bridge">
        Bay Bridge
       </a>
       , which would connect San Francisco with Oakland and the East Bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the United States joined
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       in 1941, the Bay Area became a major domestic military and naval hub, with large shipyards constructed in
       <a href="/wiki/Sausalito,_California" title="Sausalito, California">
        Sausalito
       </a>
       and across the East Bay to build ships for the war effort, and
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mason" title="Fort Mason">
        Fort Mason
       </a>
       acting the primary port of embarkation for service members shipping out to the
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatic-Pacific_Theater" title="Asiatic-Pacific Theater">
        Pacific Theater of Operations
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWII_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WWII-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the war, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       was chartered in San Francisco to help prevent the kind of devastation that occurred over the past decade,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on September 1951,
       <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">
        Japan officially surrendered
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Allied forces
       </a>
       in San Francisco, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco" title="Treaty of San Francisco">
        Treaty of San Francisco
       </a>
       entering into force a year later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the years immediately following the war, the Bay Area saw a huge wave of immigration as populations increased across the region. Between 1950 and 1960, San Francisco welcomed over 100,000 new residents, inland suburbs in the East Bay saw their populations double,
       <a href="/wiki/Daly_City,_California" title="Daly City, California">
        Daly City
       </a>
       's population quadrupled, and
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_California" title="Santa Clara, California">
        Santa Clara
       </a>
       's population quintupled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWII_42-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WWII-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco,_April_1967.jpg">
         <img alt="A pair of policemen mounted on horses observe a protest march down a street in San Francisco." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1199" data-file-width="1817" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg/220px-Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg/330px-Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg/440px-Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco%2C_April_1967.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mounted_policemen_watch_a_Vietnam_War_protest_march_in_San_Francisco,_April_1967.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mounted_police" title="Mounted police">
          Mounted policeman
         </a>
         observe a protest march against the
         <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
          Vietnam War
         </a>
         in San Francisco in 1967.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By the early 1960s, the Bay Area and the rest of
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">
        Northern California
       </a>
       became the center of the
       <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">
        counterculture movement
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Telegraph_Avenue" title="Telegraph Avenue">
        Telegraph Avenue
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">
        Berkeley
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Haight-Ashbury" title="Haight-Ashbury">
        Haight-Ashbury
       </a>
       neighborhood in San Francisco were seen as centers of activity,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashbolt_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ashbolt-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the hit American
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_song" title="Pop song">
        pop song
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_(Be_Sure_to_Wear_Flowers_in_Your_Hair)" title="San Francisco (Be Sure to Wear Flowers in Your Hair)">
         San Francisco (Be Sure to Wear Flowers in Your Hair)
        </a>
       </i>
       further enticing like-minded individuals to join the movement in the Bay Area and leading to the
       <a href="/wiki/Summer_of_Love" title="Summer of Love">
        Summer of Love
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the proceeding decades, the Bay Area would cement itself as a hotbed of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Left" title="New Left">
        New Left
       </a>
       activism,
       <a href="/wiki/Student_activism" title="Student activism">
        student activism
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opposition_to_the_Vietnam_War" title="Opposition to the Vietnam War">
        opposition to the Vietnam War
       </a>
       and other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-war_movements" title="Anti-war movements">
        anti-war movements
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Power" title="Black Power">
        black power movement
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT_social_movements" title="LGBT social movements">
        gay rights movement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ashbolt_45-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ashbolt-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the same time, San Jose and the rest of the South Bay began to rapidly develop as it began to transition from a largely agricultural-based economy into the hotbed of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-tech_industry" title="High-tech industry">
        high-tech industry
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fred_Terman" title="Fred Terman">
        Fred Terman
       </a>
       , the director of a top-secret research project at
       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">
        Harvard University
       </a>
       during World War II, joined the faculty at
       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">
        Stanford University
       </a>
       in order to reshape the university's engineering department. His students, including
       <a href="/wiki/David_Packard" title="David Packard">
        David Packard
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/William_Redington_Hewlett" title="William Redington Hewlett">
        William Hewlett
       </a>
       would later help usher in the region's high-tech revolution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWII_42-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-WWII-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1955,
       <a href="/wiki/Shockley_Semiconductor_Laboratory" title="Shockley Semiconductor Laboratory">
        Shockley Semiconductor Laboratory
       </a>
       opened for business near Stanford, and although the business venture was a financial failure, it was the first
       <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">
        semiconductor
       </a>
       company in the Bay Area, and the talent that it attracted to the region eventually led to a high-tech cluster of companies later known as
       <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">
        Silicon Valley
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg">
         <img alt="A chart displaying the NASDAQ Composite Index, including a peak in 2000 that explains the Dot-com bubble phenomenon." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="500" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg/220px-Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg/330px-Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg/440px-Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nasdaq_Composite_dot-com_bubble.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASDAQ_Composite" title="NASDAQ Composite">
          NASDAQ Composite
         </a>
         index from 1994 to 2005 showing the peak of the
         <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">
          Dot-com bubble
         </a>
         in early 2000, before collapsing.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oakland_Women%27s_March,_1-21-17_(32328542731).jpg">
         <img alt="An image of protestors marching down a street in Oakland." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg/220px-Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg/330px-Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg/440px-Oakland_Women%27s_March%2C_1-21-17_%2832328542731%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oakland_Women%27s_March,_1-21-17_(32328542731).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/2017_Women%27s_March" title="2017 Women's March">
          2017 Women's March
         </a>
         in Oakland. Other political rallies were held on the same day in numerous other locations throughout the Bay Area to spotlight
         <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">
          progressive
         </a>
         political causes and oppose the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Administration of Donald Trump">
          Presidency of Donald Trump
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1989, in the middle of the
       <a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">
        World Series
       </a>
       match between two Bay Area baseball teams, the
       <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">
        Loma Prieta earthquake
       </a>
       struck and caused widespread infrastructural damage, including the failure of the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge">
        Bay Bridge
       </a>
       , a major link between San Francisco and
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even so, the Bay Area's technology industry continued to expand and growth in Silicon Valley accelerated that the
       <a href="/wiki/1990_United_States_Census" title="1990 United States Census">
        United States Census
       </a>
       confirmed that year that San Jose had overtaken San Francisco in terms of population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The commercialization of the
       <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
        Internet
       </a>
       in the middle of the decade rapidly created a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speculative_bubble" title="Speculative bubble">
        speculative bubble
       </a>
       in the high-tech economy known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">
        Dot-com bubble
       </a>
       . This bubble began collapsing in the early 2000s and the industry continued contracting for the next few years, nearly wiping out the market. Companies like
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">
        Amazon.com
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       managed to weather the crash however, and following the industry's return to normalcy, their market value increased significantly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Even as the growth of the technology sector transformed the region's economy,
       <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">
        progressive politics
       </a>
       continued to guide the region's political environment. By the turn of the millennium,
       <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">
        Non-Hispanic whites
       </a>
       , the largest ethnic group in the United States, were only half of the population in the Bay Area as immigration among minority groups accelerated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay_Area_Census_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bay_Area_Census-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this time, the Bay Area was the center of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_movement" title="LGBT rights movement">
        LGBT rights movement
       </a>
       : in 2004, San Francisco began issuing
       <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">
        marriage licenses to same-sex couples
       </a>
       , a first in the United States,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and four years later, a majority of voters in the Bay Area rejected California
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proposition_8_(2008)" title="Proposition 8 (2008)">
        Proposition 8
       </a>
       , which sought to constitutionally restrict marriage to opposite-sex couples but ultimately passed statewide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bay Area was also the center of contentious protests concerning racial and economic inequality. In 2009, an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">
        African American
       </a>
       man named
       <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Oscar_Grant" title="Shooting of Oscar Grant">
        Oscar Grant was fatally shot
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/BART_Police" title="BART Police">
        Bay Area Rapid Transit police officers
       </a>
       , precipitating widespread protests across the region and even riots in Oakland,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and whose name was symbolically tied to the
       <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Oakland" title="Occupy Oakland">
        Occupy Oakland
       </a>
       protests two years later that sought to fight against social and economic inequality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Inauguration of Donald Trump">
        Inauguration of Donald Trump
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
        President of the United States
       </a>
       in 2017, the Bay Area became a center of resistance to his administration, beginning with widespread protests in concert with the nationwide
       <a href="/wiki/2017_Women%27s_March" title="2017 Women's March">
        Women's March
       </a>
       a day later,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       followed by frequent public feuds between Trump and various Bay Area political, cultural, and business figures over issues of race and immigration, among others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">
        Arts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Arts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Art">
        Art
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Art">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pixaranimationstudios.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of Pixar Animation Studio's headqarters." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1746" data-file-width="2792" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Pixaranimationstudios.jpg/220px-Pixaranimationstudios.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Pixaranimationstudios.jpg/330px-Pixaranimationstudios.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Pixaranimationstudios.jpg/440px-Pixaranimationstudios.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pixaranimationstudios.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pixar_Animation_Studios" title="Pixar Animation Studios">
          Pixar Animation Studios
         </a>
         , whose animated films have accrued numerous
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">
          Academy Awards
         </a>
         , is based in
         <a href="/wiki/Emeryville,_California" title="Emeryville, California">
          Emeryville
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Art_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Art in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Art in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area was, along with
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       , one of the two birthplaces of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abstract_Expressionism" title="Abstract Expressionism">
        Abstract Expressionism
       </a>
       movement of painting. It is associated with the works of
       <a href="/wiki/Clyfford_Still" title="Clyfford Still">
        Clyfford Still
       </a>
       , who began teaching at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_School_of_Fine_Arts" title="California School of Fine Arts">
        California School of Fine Arts
       </a>
       (now the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Art_Institute" title="San Francisco Art Institute">
        San Francisco Art Institute
       </a>
       ) in 1946, leaving a lasting impact on the artistic styles of Bay Area painters up to the present day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A few years later, Abstract Expressionist painter
       <a href="/wiki/David_Park_(painter)" title="David Park (painter)">
        David Park
       </a>
       painted
       <i>
        Kids on Bikes
       </i>
       in 1950, which retained many aspects of abstract expressionism but with original distinguishing features that would later lead to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Figurative_Movement" title="Bay Area Figurative Movement">
        Bay Area Figurative Movement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While both the Figurative Movement and the Abstract Expressionism movement arose from art schools,
       <a href="/wiki/Funk_art" title="Funk art">
        Funk art
       </a>
       would later rise out of the region's underground and was characterized by informal sharing of technique among groups of friends and art showcases in "cooperative" galleries instead of formal museums. Later, the Bay Area art movement would be heavily influenced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">
        counterculture movement in the 1960s
       </a>
       , and art produced during this time reflected the political environment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is presently home to a thriving computer animation industry
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pixar_Animation_Studios" title="Pixar Animation Studios">
        Pixar Animation Studios
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">
        Industrial Light &amp; Magic
       </a>
       . Pixar, based in
       <a href="/wiki/Emeryville,_California" title="Emeryville, California">
        Emeryville
       </a>
       , produced the first fully
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation#Films" title="Computer animation">
        computer animated feature film
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Toy_Story" title="Toy Story">
         Toy Story
        </a>
       </i>
       , with software it designed in-house and whose computer animation films have since garnered 26
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">
        Academy Awardss
       </a>
       and critical acclaim.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Industrial Light &amp; Magic, which is based in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidio,_San_Francisco" title="Presidio, San Francisco">
        Presidio
       </a>
       in San Francisco, was created in 1975 to help create visual effects for the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">
         Star Wars
        </a>
       </i>
       series has since been involved with creating visual effects for over three hundred Hollywood films.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_bands_from_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="List of bands from the San Francisco Bay Area">
        List of bands from the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Throughout its recent history, the Bay Area has been home to several musical movements that left lasting influences on the genres they affected. San Francisco in particular was the center of the
       <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">
        counterculture movement in the 1960s
       </a>
       , which directly led to the rise of several notable musical acts:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Grateful_Dead" title="The Grateful Dead">
        The Grateful Dead
       </a>
       , which formed in 1965, and
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Airplane" title="Jefferson Airplane">
        Jefferson Airplane
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">
        Janis Joplin
       </a>
       ; all three would be closely associated with the 1967
       <a href="/wiki/Summer_of_Love" title="Summer of Love">
        Summer of Love
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summeroflove_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-summeroflove-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">
        Jimi Hendrix
       </a>
       also had strong connections to the movement and the Bay Area, as he lived in Berkeley for a brief time as a child and played in many local venues in that decade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chroniclehistory_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chroniclehistory-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summeroflove_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-summeroflove-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 1970s, San Francisco had developed a vibrant jazz scene, earning the moniker, "Harlem of the West".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytjazz_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nytjazz-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
