        Vietnam War
       </a>
       was being fought at the time, and Bay Area bands such as
       <a href="/wiki/Creedence_Clearwater_Revival" title="Creedence Clearwater Revival">
        Creedence Clearwater Revival
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Cerrito,_California" title="El Cerrito, California">
        El Cerrito
       </a>
       became known for their political and socially-conscious lyrics
       <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_United_States_involvement_in_the_Vietnam_War" title="Opposition to United States involvement in the Vietnam War">
        against the conflict
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana" title="Carlos Santana">
        Carlos Santana
       </a>
       rose to fame in the early 1970s with his
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santana_band" title="Santana band">
        Santana band
       </a>
       and would later be inducted into the
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">
        Rock and Roll Hall of Fame
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and would later help lead the formation of the band
       <a href="/wiki/Journey_(band)" title="Journey (band)">
        Journey
       </a>
       along with former members of Santana.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 1980s and early 1990s, the Bay Area
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_thrash_metal" title="Bay Area thrash metal">
        became home to
       </a>
       one of the largest and most influential
       <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">
        thrash metal
       </a>
       scenes in the world, with contributions from acts like
       <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">
        Metallica
       </a>
       , and the emergence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde_metal" title="Avant-garde metal">
        avant-garde metal
       </a>
       with bands such as
       <a href="/wiki/Giant_Squid_(band)" title="Giant Squid (band)">
        Giant Squid
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grayceon" title="Grayceon">
        Grayceon
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ludicra" title="Ludicra">
        Ludicra
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bayarea_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bayarea-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Post-grunge" title="Post-grunge">
        post-grunge
       </a>
       era in the 1990s and featured prominent Bay Area bands
       <a href="/wiki/Third_Eye_Blind" title="Third Eye Blind">
        Third Eye Blind
       </a>
       of San Francisco,
       <a href="/wiki/Counting_Crows" title="Counting Crows">
        Counting Crows
       </a>
       of Berkeley, and
       <a href="/wiki/Smash_Mouth" title="Smash Mouth">
        Smash Mouth
       </a>
       of San Jose, and later
       <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">
        punk rock
       </a>
       bands like
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">
        Green Day
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chroniclehistory_67-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-chroniclehistory-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 1990s also saw the emergence of the influential
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyphy_movement" title="Hyphy movement">
        hyphy movement
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">
        hip hop
       </a>
       , derived from the Oakland
       <a href="/wiki/Slang" title="Slang">
        slang
       </a>
       for "hyperactive", and pioneered by Bay Area rappers
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andre_%22Mac_Dre%22_Hicks" title='Andre "Mac Dre" Hicks'>
        Andre "Mac Dre" Hicks
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mistah_Fab" title="Mistah Fab">
        Mistah Fab
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/E-40" title="E-40">
        E-40
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-definition_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-definition-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other notable rappers from the Bay Area include
       <a href="/wiki/Lil_B" title="Lil B">
        Lil B
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lilb_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lilb-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">
        Tupac Shakur
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/MC_Hammer" title="MC Hammer">
        MC Hammer
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oakrap_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-oakrap-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today, much of the rap coming out of the Oakland and the East Bay is "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conscious_rap" title="Conscious rap">
        conscious rap
       </a>
       ", which concerns itself with social issues and awareness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oakrap_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-oakrap-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is also home to hundreds of
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">
        classical music
       </a>
       ensembles, from community choirs to professional
       <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">
        orchestras
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Symphony" title="San Francisco Symphony">
        San Francisco Symphony
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California_Symphony" title="California Symphony">
        California Symphony
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Fremont Symphony Orchestra">
        Fremont Symphony Orchestra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Symphony" title="Oakland Symphony">
        Oakland Symphony
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chamber_Orchestra" title="San Francisco Chamber Orchestra">
        San Francisco Chamber Orchestra
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Theater">
        Theater
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Theater">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BerkeleyRep.jpg">
         <img alt="A picture of the Berkeley Repertory Theatre's headquarters." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="928" data-file-width="1548" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/BerkeleyRep.jpg/220px-BerkeleyRep.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/BerkeleyRep.jpg/330px-BerkeleyRep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/BerkeleyRep.jpg/440px-BerkeleyRep.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BerkeleyRep.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Repertory_Theatre" title="Berkeley Repertory Theatre">
          Berkeley Repertory Theatre
         </a>
         is one of the founding members of
         <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Bay_Area" title="Theatre Bay Area">
          Theatre Bay Area
         </a>
         and are based in a building (pictured above) in downtown
         <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">
          Berkeley
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the regional theater service organization
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Bay_Area" title="Theatre Bay Area">
        Theatre Bay Area
       </a>
       , the San Francisco Bay Area is the third largest center of activity for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theatre_company" title="Theatre company">
        theater companies
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">
        actors
       </a>
       in the United States, after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_metropolitan_area" title="New York City metropolitan area">
        New York City
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">
        Chicago metropolitan areas
       </a>
       , with 400 companies spread throughout the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The organization was founded in 1976 by the
       <a href="/wiki/Magic_Theatre" title="Magic Theatre">
        Magic Theatre
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/American_Conservatory_Theater" title="American Conservatory Theater">
        American Conservatory Theater
       </a>
       (ACT) in San Francisco and the
       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Repertory_Theatre" title="Berkeley Repertory Theatre">
        Berkeley Repertory Theatre
       </a>
       in Berkeley.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The latter two, along with the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Mime_Troupe" title="San Francisco Mime Troupe">
        San Francisco Mime Troupe
       </a>
       , have since gone on to win one
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_Theatre_Tony_Award" title="Regional Theatre Tony Award">
        Regional Theatre Tony Award
       </a>
       each.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several famous actors have arisen from the Bay Area's theatre community, including
       <a href="/wiki/Daveed_Diggs" title="Daveed Diggs">
        Daveed Diggs
       </a>
       from
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">
         Hamilton
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Darren_Criss" title="Darren Criss">
        Darren Criss
       </a>
       from
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hedwig_and_the_Angry_Inch_(musical)" title="Hedwig and the Angry Inch (musical)">
         Hedwig
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/A_Very_Potter_Musical" title="A Very Potter Musical">
         A Very Potter Musical
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">
         Glee
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Locally, well-regarded actors include
       <a href="/wiki/James_Carpenter_(actor)" title="James Carpenter (actor)">
        James Carpenter
       </a>
       , a stage actor who has performed at the ACT, Berkeley Repertory, and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Repertory_Theatre" title="San Jose Repertory Theatre">
        San Jose Repertory Theatre
       </a>
       among others, Rod Gnapp of the Magic Theatre Company, Sean San Jose, one of the founders of the Campo Santo theater, and Campo Santo member Margo Hall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area also has an active youth theater scene. ACT and the Berkeley Repertory both run classes and camps for young actors, as do the Peninsula Youth Theater and Willow Glen Children’s Theatre in the Peninsula and South Bay, Bay Area Children's Theater and Danville Children’s Musical Theater in the East Bay, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marin_Shakespeare" title="Marin Shakespeare">
        Marin Shakespeare
       </a>
       in the North Bay, among many others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Media in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Media in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chronicle_Building,_San_Francisco,_1901.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of the Old Chronicle Building." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="988" data-file-width="602" height="361" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg/220px-Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg/330px-Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg/440px-Chronicle_Building%2C_San_Francisco%2C_1901.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chronicle_Building,_San_Francisco,_1901.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Ritz-Carlton_Club_and_Residences" title="Ritz-Carlton Club and Residences">
          Old Chronicle Building
         </a>
         , which housed the offices of the
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">
           San Francisco Chronicle
          </a>
         </i>
         until 1924.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The San Francisco Bay Area is the sixth-largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" title="Designated market area">
        television market
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the fourth-largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" title="Designated market area">
        radio market
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the U.S. The Bay Aea's oldest radio station,
       <a href="/wiki/KCBS_(AM)" title="KCBS (AM)">
        KCBS (AM)
       </a>
       , began as an experimental station in San Jose in 1909, before the beginning of commercial broadcasting.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/KALW" title="KALW">
        KALW
       </a>
       was the Bay Area's first
       <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">
        FM radio station
       </a>
       , and first radio station to begin commercial broadcasting west of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       when it signed on the air in 1941.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KPIX" title="KPIX">
        KPIX
       </a>
       , which began broadcasting in 1948, was the first television station to air in the Bay Area and Northern California.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       All major U.S. television networks have
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="List of television stations in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        affiliates
       </a>
       serving the region, including
       <a href="/wiki/KTVU" title="KTVU">
        KTVU
       </a>
       2 (FOX),
       <a href="/wiki/KRON-TV" title="KRON-TV">
        KRON-TV
       </a>
       4 (myNetworkTV),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KPIX" title="KPIX">
        KPIX
       </a>
       5 (CBS),
       <a href="/wiki/KGO-TV" title="KGO-TV">
        KGO-TV
       </a>
       7 (ABC),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KQED-TV" title="KQED-TV">
        KQED-TV
       </a>
       9 (PBS),
       <a href="/wiki/KNTV" title="KNTV">
        KNTV
       </a>
       11 (NBC),
       <a href="/wiki/KBCW_(TV)" title="KBCW (TV)">
        KBCW
       </a>
       44/45 (CW),
       <a href="/wiki/KQEH" title="KQEH">
        KQEH
       </a>
       54 (PBS), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KKPX" title="KKPX">
        KKPX
       </a>
       65 (
       <a href="/wiki/Ion_Television" title="Ion Television">
        Ion
       </a>
       ).
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloomberg_West" title="Bloomberg West">
        Bloomberg West
       </a>
       , a show that focuses on topics pertaining to technology and business, was launched in 2011 from a studio in and continues to broadcast from San Francisco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">
        Public broadcasting
       </a>
       outlets include both a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KQED-TV" title="KQED-TV">
        television station
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/KQED-FM" title="KQED-FM">
        radio station
       </a>
       , both broadcasting under the call letters KQED from a facility near the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Potrero_Hill,_San_Francisco" title="Potrero Hill, San Francisco">
        Potrero Hill
       </a>
       neighborhood. KQED-FM is the most-listened-to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">
        National Public Radio
       </a>
       affiliate in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another local broadcaster,
       <a href="/wiki/KPOO" title="KPOO">
        KPOO
       </a>
       , is an independent, African-American owned and operated noncommercial radio station established in 1971.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest newspapers in the Bay Area are the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">
         San Francisco Chronicle
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Jose_Mercury_News" title="San Jose Mercury News">
         San Jose Mercury News
        </a>
       </i>
       , the highest and second-highest most widely circulated newspaper in
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">
        Northern California
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        The Chronicle
       </i>
       is most famous for a former columnist, the late
       <a href="/wiki/Herb_Caen" title="Herb Caen">
        Herb Caen
       </a>
       , whose daily musings attracted critical acclaim and represented the "voice of San Francisco". The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Examiner" title="San Francisco Examiner">
         San Francisco Examiner
        </a>
       </i>
       , once the cornerstone of
       <a href="/wiki/William_Randolph_Hearst" title="William Randolph Hearst">
        William Randolph Hearst
       </a>
       's media empire and the home of
       <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Bierce" title="Ambrose Bierce">
        Ambrose Bierce
       </a>
       , declined in circulation over the years and now takes the form of a free daily tabloid, under new ownership.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of the Bay Area's local regions and municipalities also have their own newspapers, such as the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Bay_Times" title="East Bay Times">
         East Bay Times
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo_Daily_Journal" title="San Mateo Daily Journal">
         San Mateo Daily Journal
        </a>
       </i>
       . The national newsmagazine
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mother_Jones_(magazine)" title="Mother Jones (magazine)">
         Mother Jones
        </a>
       </i>
       is also based in San Francisco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Non-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_(language)" title="English (language)">
        English
       </a>
       language newspapers include several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_(language)" title="Chinese (language)">
        Chinese
       </a>
       -language papers such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sing_Tao_Daily" title="Sing Tao Daily">
         Sing Tao Daily
        </a>
       </i>
       , the largest in the Bay Area by circulation,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <i>
        El Mundo
       </i>
       , a free
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_(language)" title="Spanish (language)">
        Spanish
       </a>
       -language weekly distributed by the
       <i>
        Mercury News
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_recreation">
        Sports and recreation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sports and recreation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Sports in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Sports in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AT%26T_Park_July_24,_2016.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of AT&amp;T Park, a baseball field" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg/220px-AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg/330px-AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg/440px-AT%26T_Park_July_24%2C_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AT%26T_Park_July_24,_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Park" title="AT&amp;T Park">
          AT&amp;T Park
         </a>
         , home to the
         <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">
          San Francisco Giants
         </a>
         , is situated along the waterfront and has a view of the
         <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
          San Francisco Bay
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg/220px-Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg/330px-Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg/440px-Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cyclists_Above_Grant_Ranch.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A paceline of
         <a href="/wiki/Drafting_(aerodynamics)" title="Drafting (aerodynamics)">
          drafting
         </a>
         cyclists while ascending
         <a href="/wiki/Mount_Hamilton_(California)" title="Mount Hamilton (California)">
          Mount Hamilton
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">
          Santa Clara county
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is home to seven professional major league sports franchises: The
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">
        San Francisco 49ers
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" title="Oakland Raiders">
        Oakland Raiders
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        National Football League
       </a>
       (NFL) in
       <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">
        American football
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">
        San Francisco Giants
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">
        Oakland Athletics
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       (MLB), the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">
        Golden State Warriors
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       (NBA), the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Sharks" title="San Jose Sharks">
        San Jose Sharks
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        National Hockey League
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Earthquakes" title="San Jose Earthquakes">
        San Jose Earthquakes
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">
        Major League Soccer
       </a>
       . In
       <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">
        sailing
       </a>
       , the Bay Area was host to the
       <a href="/wiki/2013_America%27s_Cup" title="2013 America's Cup">
        2013 America's Cup
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In American football, the 49ers play in
       <a href="/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium" title="Levi's Stadium">
        Levi's Stadium
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and have won five
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">
        Super Bowls
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XVI" title="Super Bowl XVI">
        XVI
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIX" title="Super Bowl XIX">
        XIX
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXIII" title="Super Bowl XXIII">
        XXIII
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXIV" title="Super Bowl XXIV">
        XXIV
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXIX" title="Super Bowl XXIX">
        XXIX
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) and lost one (XLVII
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), while the Raiders play in
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland%E2%80%93Alameda_County_Coliseum" title="Oakland–Alameda County Coliseum">
        Oakland–Alameda County Coliseum
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcoliseum_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aboutcoliseum-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       until their
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders_relocation_to_Las_Vegas" title="Oakland Raiders relocation to Las Vegas">
        relocation
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">
        Las Vegas
       </a>
       in either 2019 or 2020
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and have won three Super Bowls (
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XI" title="Super Bowl XI">
        XI
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XV" title="Super Bowl XV">
        XV
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XVIII" title="Super Bowl XVIII">
        XVIII
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), and lost two (
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_II" title="Super Bowl II">
        II
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVII" title="Super Bowl XXXVII">
        XXXVII
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) In baseball, the San Francisco Giants, who play at
       <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Park" title="AT&amp;T Park">
        AT&amp;T Park
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       have won eight
       <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">
        World Series
       </a>
       titles,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldseries_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-worldseries-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the Oakland Athletics, who share the Oakland Coliseum with the Raiders,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcoliseum_105-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aboutcoliseum-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       have won nine World Series titles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldseries_113-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-worldseries-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        basketball
       </a>
       , the Warriors play in
       <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Arena" title="Oracle Arena">
        Oracle Arena
       </a>
       and have won three
       <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">
        NBA Finals
       </a>
       since their move to Oakland in 1971.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">
        hockey
       </a>
       , the Sharks play at the
       <a href="/wiki/SAP_Center" title="SAP Center">
        SAP Center
       </a>
       and have yet to win the
       <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">
        Stanley Cup
       </a>
       despite making their first
       <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="Stanley Cup Finals">
        Stanley Cup Finals
       </a>
       appearance in
       <a href="/wiki/2016_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="2016 Stanley Cup Finals">
        2016
       </a>
       . In
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        soccer
       </a>
       , the Earthquakes play at
       <a href="/wiki/Avaya_Stadium" title="Avaya Stadium">
        Avaya Stadium
       </a>
       and have won the
       <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup" title="MLS Cup">
        MLS Cup
       </a>
       twice in
       <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2001" title="MLS Cup 2001">
        2001
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/MLS_Cup_2003" title="MLS Cup 2003">
        2003
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Outside of major league sports, the Bay Area is home to seven minor league teams: one soccer team (
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Deltas" title="San Francisco Deltas">
        San Francisco Deltas
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       one hockey team (
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Barracuda" title="San Jose Barracuda">
        San Jose Barracuda
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       one
       <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">
        Minor League Baseball
       </a>
       team (
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Giants" title="San Jose Giants">
        San Jose Giants
       </a>
       ) in the
       <a href="/wiki/California_League" title="California League">
        California League
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and four baseball teams in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Association_of_Professional_Baseball_Clubs" title="Pacific Association of Professional Baseball Clubs">
        Pacific Association of Professional Baseball Clubs
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/San_Rafael_Pacifics" title="San Rafael Pacifics">
        San Rafael Pacifics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_Stompers" title="Sonoma Stompers">
        Sonoma Stompers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pittsburg_Diamonds" title="Pittsburg Diamonds">
        Pittsburg Diamonds
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo_Admirals" title="Vallejo Admirals">
        Vallejo Admirals
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In terms of collegiate sports, six Bay Area universities are members of
       <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
        NCAA
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">
        Division I
       </a>
       , the highest level of college sports in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All three football-playing schools in the Bay Area are in the
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">
        Football Bowl Subdivision
       </a>
       , the highest level of NCAA
       <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">
        college football
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears" title="California Golden Bears">
        California Golden Bears
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal" title="Stanford Cardinal">
        Stanford Cardinal
       </a>
       compete in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pac-12_Conference" title="Pac-12 Conference">
        Pac-12 Conference
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_Spartans" title="San Jose State Spartans">
        San Jose State Spartans
       </a>
       compete in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_West_Conference" title="Mountain West Conference">
        Mountain West Conference
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Cardinal and Golden Bears are intense rivals, with their football teams competing annually in the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Game_(American_football)" title="Big Game (American football)">
        Big Game
       </a>
       for the Stanford Axe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the most famous games in the rivalry occurred in 1982, when the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears_football" title="California Golden Bears football">
        Golden Bears
       </a>
       defeated the
       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal_football" title="Stanford Cardinal football">
        Cardinal
       </a>
       on a last-second return kickoff known as "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Play_(Stanford_vs._California)" title="The Play (Stanford vs. California)">
        The Play
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area has an ideal climate for outdoor recreation, such that activities like hiking and cycling are popular among locals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are more than 200 miles (320 km) of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities">
        bicycle paths, lanes
       </a>
       and bike routes just within San Francisco,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Embarcadero_(San_Francisco)" title="Embarcadero (San Francisco)">
        Embarcadero
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marina_Green" title="Marina Green">
        Marina Green
       </a>
       are favored sites for
       <a href="/wiki/Skateboarding" title="Skateboarding">
        skateboarding
       </a>
       . Extensive public tennis facilities are available in
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Park" title="Golden Gate Park">
        Golden Gate Park
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolores_Park" title="Dolores Park">
        Dolores Park
       </a>
       , as well as at smaller neighborhood courts throughout the city. San Francisco residents have often ranked among the fittest in the U.S.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitness_127-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fitness-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Boating, sailing,
       <a href="/wiki/Windsurfing" title="Windsurfing">
        windsurfing
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" title="Kitesurfing">
        kitesurfing
       </a>
       are among the popular activities on San Francisco Bay, and the city maintains a yacht harbor in the
       <a href="/wiki/Marina_District,_San_Francisco" title="Marina District, San Francisco">
        Marina District
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/St._Francis_Yacht_Club" title="St. Francis Yacht Club">
        St. Francis Yacht Club
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Yacht_Club" title="Golden Gate Yacht Club">
        Golden Gate Yacht Club
       </a>
       are located in the Marina Harbor,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while the South Beach Yacht Club is located next to AT&amp;T Park.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_Tet_parade,_2009.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of members of the Vietnamese community marching in San Jose" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1393" data-file-width="2068" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg/220px-San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg/330px-San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg/440px-San_Jose_Tet_parade%2C_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_Tet_parade,_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
          San Jose
         </a>
         is home to the largest Vietnamese community outside of
         <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">
          Vietnam
         </a>
         . Here, the Vietnamese diaspora celebrate
         <a href="/wiki/T%E1%BA%BFt" title="Tết">
          Tết
         </a>
         , or New Years, in San Jose.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

        <div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">

         <span style="color:#ff0000">

         ,
         <span style="color:#0000ff">
          African
         </span>
         ,
         <span style="color:#00ff80">
          Asian
         </span>
         ,
         <span style="color:#ff8000">
          Hispanic
         </span>
         , or Other (yellow)
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco,_Oakland,_Berkeley_(5560477152).png">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="3009" data-file-width="3009" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png/200px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png/300px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png/400px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_San_Francisco%2C_Oakland%2C_Berkeley_%285560477152%29.png 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          San Francisco and Oakland
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg/200px-San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg/300px-San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg/400px-San_Jose_Demographics_2010.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          San Jose
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 United States Census
       </a>
       , the population of the nine-county Bay Area was 7.15 million, with 49.6% male and 50.4% female.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay_Area_Census_52-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bay_Area_Census-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of these, approximately 2.3 million (32%) are foreign born.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010 the racial makeup of the nine-county Bay Area was 52.5%
       <a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">
        White
       </a>
       of which 42.4% were
       <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">
        non-Hispanic
       </a>
       and 10.1% were
       <a href="/wiki/White_Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="White Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanic
       </a>
       , 23.5%
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanic or Latino
       </a>
       of any race (17.9% Mexican, 1.3% Salvadoran, 0.6% Guatemalan, 0.6% Puerto Rican, 0.5% Nicaraguan, 0.3% Peruvian, 0.2% Cuban), 23.3%
       <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">
        Asian
       </a>
       (7.9% Chinese, 5.1% Filipino, 3.3% Indian, 2.5% Vietnamese, 1.0% Korean, 0.9% Japanese, 0.2% Pakistani, 0.2% Cambodian, 0.2% Laotian, 0.1% Thai, 0.1% Burmese), 6.7% non-Hispanic
       <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">
        African American
       </a>
       , 0.7%
       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
        Native American
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Natives" title="Alaska Natives">
        Alaska Native
       </a>
       , 0.6%
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Americans" title="Pacific Islands Americans">
        Pacific Islander
       </a>
       (0.1% Tongan, 0.1% Samoan, 0.1% Fijian, &gt;0.1% Guamanian, &gt;0.1% Native Hawaiian), 5.4% from
       <a href="/wiki/Multiracial_Americans" title="Multiracial Americans">
        two or more races
       </a>
       and 10.8% from other races.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanfactfinder_133-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-americanfactfinder-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bay Area cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suisun_City,_California" title="Suisun City, California">
        Suisun City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Leandro,_California" title="San Leandro, California">
        San Leandro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_California" title="Fairfield, California">
        Fairfield
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
        Richmond
       </a>
       are among the most ethnically diverse cities in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BusinessInsider_134-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BusinessInsider-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Based on geographic location,
       <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">
        non-Hispanic whites
       </a>
       make up the majority in
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">
        Marin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Napa_County,_California" title="Napa County, California">
        Napa
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_County,_California" title="Sonoma County, California">
        Sonoma counties
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay_Area_Census_52-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bay_Area_Census-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Whites also make up the majority in the eastern regions of the
       <a href="/wiki/East_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="East Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        East Bay
       </a>
       centered around
       <a href="/wiki/Livermore,_California" title="Livermore, California">
        Livermore
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Walnut_Creek,_California" title="Walnut Creek, California">
        Walnut Creek
       </a>
       areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay_Area_Census_52-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bay_Area_Census-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       San Francisco's
       <a href="/wiki/North_Beach,_San_Francisco" title="North Beach, San Francisco">
        North Beach
       </a>
       district is considered the
       <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy" title="Little Italy">
        Little Italy
       </a>
       of the city, and was once home to a significant Italian American community. San Francisco and Marin County both have substantial
       <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">
        Jewish
       </a>
       communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asarb_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-asarb-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">
        Latino
       </a>
       population is spread throughout the Bay Area, but among the nine counties, the greatest number of them live in Santa Clara County, while Contra Costa County sees the highest growth rate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Americans" title="Mexican Americans">
        Mexican Americans
       </a>
       make up the largest share of Hispanic residents in Napa county,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while Central Americans make up the largest share in San Francisco, many of whom live in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mission_District,_San_Francisco" title="Mission District, San Francisco">
        Mission District
       </a>
       which is home to many residents of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvadoran_American" title="Salvadoran American">
        Salvadoran
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guatemalan_American" title="Guatemalan American">
        Guatemalan
       </a>
       descent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Asian_Americans" title="Asian Americans">
        Asian American
       </a>
       population in the Bay Area is significant compared to other regions in the U.S., concentrated in the Bay Area city of
       <a href="/wiki/Daly_City,_California" title="Daly City, California">
        Daly City
       </a>
       . At 58.4%, Daly City's Asian American population is larger than anywhere else in the United States outside of
       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
        Hawaii
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Asian Americans also constitute a majority in
       <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_California" title="Fremont, California">
        Fremont
       </a>
       , with significant populations in
       <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California" title="Sunnyvale, California">
        Sunnyvale
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_California" title="Santa Clara, California">
        Santa Clara
       </a>
       . The cities of San Jose and San Francisco had the third and fourth largest total number of Asian Americans out of every American city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans" title="Chinese Americans">
        Chinese Americans
       </a>
       constitute 21.4% of the population and constitute the single largest ethnic group in the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Santa Clara county, and increasingly the East Bay, house a significant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_American" title="Indian American">
        Indian American
       </a>
       community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bay Area is home to over 382,950
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_American" title="Filipino American">
        Filipino Americans
       </a>
       , one of the largest communities of Filipino people outside of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       with the largest proportion of Filipino Americans concentrating themselves within
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Canyon" title="American Canyon">
        American Canyon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Daly_City,_California" title="Daly City, California">
        Daly City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_California" title="Fairfield, California">
        Fairfield
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South_San_Francisco,_California" title="South San Francisco, California">
        South San Francisco
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are more than 100,000 people of
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Americans" title="Vietnamese Americans">
        Vietnamese
       </a>
       ancestry residing within
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
        San Jose
       </a>
       city limits, the largest Vietnamese population of any city in the world outside of
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">
        Vietnam
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, there is a sizable community of
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_Americans" title="Korean Americans">
        Korean Americans
       </a>
       in Santa Clara county, where San Jose is located.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       East Bay cities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
        Richmond
       </a>
       and Oakland, and the North Bay city of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa,_California" title="Santa Rosa, California">
        Santa Rosa
       </a>
       , have plentiful populations of
       <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Americans" title="Laotian Americans">
        Laotian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Americans" title="Cambodian Americans">
        Cambodians
       </a>
       in certain neighborhoods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">
        Pacific Islanders
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Americans" title="Samoan Americans">
        Samoans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tongan_Americans" title="Tongan Americans">
        Tongans
       </a>
       have the largest presence in
       <a href="/wiki/East_Palo_Alto,_California" title="East Palo Alto, California">
        East Palo Alto
       </a>
       , where they constitute over 7% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_147-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">
        African American
       </a>
       population of the Bay Area used to be significant in San Francisco, where one out of seven residents were black in 1970, which had a thriving
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       scene and was known as "Harlem of the West". Today, they have mostly moved to parts of the East Bay and North Bay, including the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Antioch,_California" title="Antioch, California">
        Antioch
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytjazz_68-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nytjazz-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The South Park neighborhood of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa,_California" title="Santa Rosa, California">
        Santa Rosa
       </a>
       was home to once a primarily black community until the 1980s, when many Latino immigrants settled in the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-southpark_148-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-southpark-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other cities with large numbers of African Americans include
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       (28%),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
        Richmond
       </a>
       (26%),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and East Palo Alto (17%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_147-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EPA-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is one of the wealthiest regions in the United States, due, primarily, to the economic power engines of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
        San Jose
       </a>
       , San Francisco, and
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       . The Bay Area city of
       <a href="/wiki/Pleasanton,_California" title="Pleasanton, California">
        Pleasanton
       </a>
       has the second-highest household income in the country after
       <a href="/wiki/New_Canaan,_Connecticut" title="New Canaan, Connecticut">
        New Canaan, Connecticut
       </a>
       . However, discretionary income is very comparable with the rest of the country, primarily because the higher cost of living offsets the increased income.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-affluence_151-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-affluence-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 2014, the Bay Area's wealth gap was considerable: the top ten percent of income-earners took home over eleven times as much as the bottom ten percent,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wealthinequality_152-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wealthinequality-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">
        Brookings Institution
       </a>
       study found the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland%E2%80%93Hayward,_CA_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="San Francisco–Oakland–Hayward, CA Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        San Francisco metro area
       </a>
       , which excludes four Bay Area counties, to be the third most unequal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        urban area
       </a>
       in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Among the wealthy, there are forty-seven Bay Area residents made the
       <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">
        Forbes
       </a>
       magazine's 400 richest Americans list, published in 2007. Thirteen lived in San Francisco proper, placing it seventh among cities in the world. Among the forty-seven were several well-known names such as
       <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">
        Steve Jobs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">
        George Lucas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_R._Schwab" title="Charles R. Schwab">
        Charles Schwab
       </a>
       . The wealthiest resident was
       <a href="/wiki/Larry_Ellison" title="Larry Ellison">
        Larry Ellison
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">
        Oracle
       </a>
       , worth $25 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A study by
       <a href="/wiki/Capgemini" title="Capgemini">
        Capgemini
       </a>
       indicates that in 2009, 4.5 percent of all households within the San Francisco-Oakland and San Jose metropolitan areas held $1 million in investable assets, placing the region first in the United States, just ahead of the New York City metro region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the other hand, low income residents in the Bay Area saw their incomes fall by nine percent since 2007, with the bottom ten percent earning just $20,000 on average.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wealthinequality_152-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wealthinequality-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        </td>

        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>
