      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Crime">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Statistics regarding crime rates in the Bay Area generally fall into two categories:
       <a href="/wiki/Violent_crime" title="Violent crime">
        violent crime
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Property_crime" title="Property crime">
        property crime
       </a>
       . Historically, violent crime has been concentrated in a few cities in the East Bay, namely
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">
        Oakland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
        Richmond
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Antioch,_California" title="Antioch, California">
        Antioch
       </a>
       , but also
       <a href="/wiki/East_Palo_Alto,_California" title="East Palo Alto, California">
        East Palo Alto
       </a>
       in the Peninsula,
       <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">
        Vallejo
       </a>
       in the North Bay, and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uneven_156-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-uneven-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nationally, Oakland's murder rate ranked 18th among cities with over 100,000 residents, and third for violent crimes per capita.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbireport_157-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fbireport-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to a 2015
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">
        Federal Bureau of Investigation
       </a>
       report, Oakland was also the source of the most violent crime in the Bay Area, with 16.9 reported incidents per thousand people. Vallejo came in second, at 8.7 incidents per thousand people, while San Pablo, Antioch, and San Francisco rounded out the top five. East Palo Alto, which used to have the Bay Area's highest murder rate, saw violent crime incidents drop 65% between 2013 and 2014, while Oakland saw violent crime incidents drop 15%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uneven_156-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-uneven-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Meanwhile,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">
        San Jose
       </a>
       , which was one of the safest large cities in the United States in the early 2000s, has seen its violent crime rates trend upwards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cities with the lowest rate of violent crime include the Peninsula cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos,_California" title="Los Altos, California">
        Los Altos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Foster_City,_California" title="Foster City, California">
        Foster City
       </a>
       , East Bay cities of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Ramon,_California" title="San Ramon, California">
        San Ramon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Danville,_California" title="Danville, California">
        Danville
       </a>
       , and South Bay cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Saratoga,_California" title="Saratoga, California">
        Saratoga
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cupertino,_California" title="Cupertino, California">
        Cupertino
       </a>
       . In 2015, 45 Bay Area cities counted zero homicides, the largest of which was
       <a href="/wiki/Daly_City,_California" title="Daly City, California">
        Daly City
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uneven_156-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-uneven-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015, Oakland also saw the highest rates of property crime in the Bay Area, at 59.4 incidents per thousand residents, with San Francisco following close behind at 53 incidents per thousand residents. The East Bay cities
       <a href="/wiki/Pleasant_Hill,_California" title="Pleasant Hill, California">
        Pleasant Hill
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">
        Berkeley
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Leandro,_California" title="San Leandro, California">
        San Leandro
       </a>
       rounded out the top five. The South Bay city of
       <a href="/wiki/Saratoga,_California" title="Saratoga, California">
        Saratoga
       </a>
       and the North Bay city of
       <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_California" title="Windsor, California">
        Windsor
       </a>
       saw the least rates of property crime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uneven_156-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-uneven-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, San Francisco saw the most reports of arson.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbireport_157-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-fbireport-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several street gangs operate in the Bay Area, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Sure%C3%B1os" title="Sureños">
        Sureños
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Norte%C3%B1os" title="Norteños">
        Norteños
       </a>
       in San Francisco's
       <a href="/wiki/Mission_District,_San_Francisco" title="Mission District, San Francisco">
        Mission District
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       African-American street gangs familiar in other cities, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">
        Crips
       </a>
       , have struggled to establish footholds in the city,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although gangs with shotcallers in China, including
       <a href="/wiki/Triad_(organized_crime)" title="Triad (organized crime)">
        Triad
       </a>
       groups such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Wo_Hop_To" title="Wo Hop To">
        Wo Hop To
       </a>
       , have been reported active.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1977, an ongoing rivalry between two Chinese gangs led to a
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Dragon_massacre" title="Golden Dragon massacre">
        shooting attack at the Golden Dragon restaurant in Chinatown
       </a>
       , which left five people dead and eleven wounded. Five members of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joe_Boys" title="Joe Boys">
        Joe Boys
       </a>
       gang were arrested and convicted of the crime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Oakland, which also sees organized gang violence, implemented
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ceasefire" title="Operation Ceasefire">
        Operation Ceasefire
       </a>
       in 2012 in an effort to reduce the violence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Googleplex_(4842867784).jpg">
         <img alt="An image of Google's corporate headquarters." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg/220px-Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg/330px-Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg/440px-Googleplex_%284842867784%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Googleplex_(4842867784).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
          Google
         </a>
         , a
         <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">
          multinational
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">
          technology company
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">
          subsidiary
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">
          Alphabet Inc.
         </a>
         , is headquartered in the Bay Area city of
         <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">
          Mountain View
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The three principal cities of the Bay Area represent different employment clusters and are dominated by different, but commingled, industries. San Francisco is home to the region's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_industry" title="Financial industry">
        financial
       </a>
       and business industry, tourism, and is host to numerous conventions. The East Bay, centered around Oakland, is home to heavy industry, metalworking, oil, and shipping, while Silicon Valley is a major pole of economic activity around the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-tech" title="High-tech">
        technology
       </a>
       industry. Furthermore, the North Bay is a major player in the country's
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agriculture
       </a>
       and wine industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-walker_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-walker-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In all, the Bay Area is home to the second highest concentration of
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       companies, second only to the
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">
        New York metropolitan area
       </a>
       , with thirty such companies based throughout the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, the greater
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Jose-San_Francisco-Oakland,_CA_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="San Jose-San Francisco-Oakland, CA Combined Statistical Area">
        twelve-county statistical area
       </a>
       had a GDP of $820.9 billion, the third-highest among
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_areas" title="Combined statistical areas">
        combined statistical areas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The smaller nine-county Bay Area had a GDP of $781 billion, which nonetheless would rank it 5th
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_GDP" title="List of U.S. states by GDP">
        among U.S. states
       </a>
       and 18th
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">
        among countries
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several major corporations are headquartered in the Bay Area. Among the Fortune 500 companies located in the region include technology companies
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">
        Apple Inc.
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard" title="Hewlett Packard">
        Hewlett Packard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
        Intel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Applied_Materials" title="Applied Materials">
        Applied Materials
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">
        eBay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">
        Cisco Systems
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Symantec" title="Symantec">
        Symantec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">
        Oracle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">
        Netflix
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salesforce" title="Salesforce">
        Salesforce
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">
        energy
       </a>
       companies
       <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">
        Chevron
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PG%26E" title="PG&amp;E">
        PG&amp;E
       </a>
       ; financial service companies
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Schwab_Corporation" title="Charles Schwab Corporation">
        Charles Schwab Corporation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">
        Visa Inc.
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">
        Wells Fargo
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apparel" title="Apparel">
        apparel
       </a>
       retailers
       <a href="/wiki/Gap_Inc." title="Gap Inc.">
        Gap Inc.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Levi_Strauss_%26_Co." title="Levi Strauss &amp; Co.">
        Levi Strauss &amp; Co.
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ross_Stores" title="Ross Stores">
        Ross Stores
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">
        aerospace
       </a>
       and defense contractor
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       ; local
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grocer" title="Grocer">
        grocer
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Safeway_Inc." title="Safeway Inc.">
        Safeway
       </a>
       ; pharmaceutical company
       <a href="/wiki/McKesson_Corporation" title="McKesson Corporation">
        McKesson
       </a>
       ; and biotechnology companies
       <a href="/wiki/Genentech" title="Genentech">
        Genentech
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gilead_Sciences" title="Gilead Sciences">
        Gilead Sciences
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The largest manufacturers include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tesla_Inc." title="Tesla Inc.">
        Tesla Inc.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lam_Research" title="Lam Research">
        Lam Research
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bayer" title="Bayer">
        Bayer
       </a>
       , Chevron, and
       <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">
        Coca-Cola
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Oakland is the site of the fifth-largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Container_terminal" title="Container terminal">
        container shipping port
       </a>
       in the United States and is also a major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_terminus" title="Rail terminus">
        rail terminus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-North_America_Container_Traffic_Rankings_169-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-North_America_Container_Traffic_Rankings-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In research,
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Ames_Research_Center" title="NASA Ames Research Center">
        Ames Research Center
       </a>
       and the federal research facility
       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Livermore_National_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory">
        Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory
       </a>
       are based in
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">
        Mountain View
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Livermore,_California" title="Livermore, California">
        Livermore
       </a>
       respectively. In the North Bay, Napa and Sonoma counties are known for their famous wineries, including
       <a href="/wiki/Fantesca_Estate_%26_Winery" title="Fantesca Estate &amp; Winery">
        Fantesca Estate &amp; Winery
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Domaine_Chandon_California" title="Domaine Chandon California">
        Domaine Chandon California
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/D%27Agostini_Winery" title="D'Agostini Winery">
        D'Agostini Winery
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The strong economic growth has created hundreds of thousands of new jobs, and this fact, coupled with severe restrictions on building new housing units,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seattle_vs._S.F._housing_171-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Seattle_vs._S.F._housing-171">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
       has resulted in an extreme housing shortage. For example, from 2012 to 2017, the San Francisco metropolitan area added 400,000 new jobs, but only 60,000 new housing units.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-homes_where_the_jobs_are_172-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-homes_where_the_jobs_are-172">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2016, the entire Bay Area had 3.6 M jobs, and 2.6 M housing units, for a ratio of 1.4 jobs per housing unit,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BA_jobs_to_housing_units_173-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BA_jobs_to_housing_units-173">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
       significantly above the ratio for the US as a whole, which stands at 1.1 jobs per housing unit. (152M jobs, 136M housing units
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US-Census-Housing_Units_175-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-US-Census-Housing_Units-175">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) As of 2017, the average income needed in order to purchase a house in the region was $179,390, while the median price for a house was $895,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
        <a href="#cite_note-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of the high cost of housing, many workers in the Bay Area live far from their place of employment, contributing to one of the highest percentages of
       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_commuting" title="Extreme commuting">
        extreme commuters
       </a>
       in the United States, or commutes that take over ninety minutes in one direction. For example, about 50,000 people commute from neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_County,_California" title="San Joaquin County, California">
        San Joaquin county
       </a>
       into the nine-county Bay Area daily,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and more extremely, some workers commute daily by flying.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
        Colleges and universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="List of colleges and universities in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        List of colleges and universities in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of UC Berkeley's campus." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="1024" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg/220px-UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg/330px-UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg/440px-UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UCBerkeleyCampus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Memorial Glade of Sather Tower in the
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">
          University of California, Berkeley
         </a>
         campus. Berkeley is the highest-ranked public university in the United States, according to
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report">
           US News &amp; World Report
          </a>
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is home to a large number of colleges and universities. The first institution of higher education in the Bay Area,
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_University" title="Santa Clara University">
        Santa Clara University
       </a>
       , was founded by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">
        Jesuits
       </a>
       in 1851,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
        <a href="#cite_note-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who also founded the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco" title="University of San Francisco">
        University of San Francisco
       </a>
       in 1855.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
        <a href="#cite_note-180">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">
        San Jose State University
       </a>
       was founded in 1857 and is the oldest public college on the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">
        West Coast of the United States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">
        Brookings Institution
       </a>
       , 45% of residents of the two-county San Jose metro area have a college degree and 43% of residents in the five-county San Francisco metro area have a college degree, the second and fourth highest ranked metro areas in the country for higher educational attainment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rankings compiled by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">
         U.S. News &amp; World Report
        </a>
       </i>
       feature several Bay Area universities in prominent spots.
       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">
        Stanford University
       </a>
       is the highest ranked university in the Bay Area, and fifth overall in the United States. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">
        University of California, Berkeley
       </a>
       is ranked twentieth overall, but for the past nineteen years has been highest-ranked public university in the country. Additionally,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">
        San Jose State University
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_State_University" title="Sonoma State University">
        Sonoma State University
       </a>
       were respectively ranked sixth and tenth among public colleges in the West Coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city of San Francisco is host to two additional
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">
        University of California
       </a>
       schools, neither of which confer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undergraduate" title="Undergraduate">
        undergraduate
       </a>
       degrees. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Francisco" title="University of California, San Francisco">
        University of California, San Francisco
       </a>
       is entirely dedicated to graduate education in health and biomedical sciences. It is ranked among the top five medical schools in the United States
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and operates the
       <a href="/wiki/UCSF_Medical_Center" title="UCSF Medical Center">
        UCSF Medical Center
       </a>
       , which is the highest-ranked hopsital in California.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
        <a href="#cite_note-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Hastings_College_of_the_Law" title="University of California, Hastings College of the Law">
        University of California, Hastings College of the Law
       </a>
       , founded in
       <a href="/wiki/Civic_Center,_San_Francisco" title="Civic Center, San Francisco">
        Civic Center
       </a>
       in 1878, is the oldest law school in California and claims more judges on the state bench than any other institution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
        <a href="#cite_note-186">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city is also host to a
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_University" title="California State University">
        California State University
       </a>
       school,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_State_University" title="San Francisco State University">
        San Francisco State University
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfsu_187-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sfsu-187">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/California_Community_Colleges_System" title="California Community Colleges System">
        California Community Colleges System
       </a>
       also operates a number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Community_colleges" title="Community colleges">
        community colleges
       </a>
       in the Bay Area. According to
       <a href="/wiki/CNNMoney" title="CNNMoney">
        CNNMoney
       </a>
       , the Bay Area community college with the highest "success" rate is
       <a href="/wiki/De_Anza_College" title="De Anza College">
        De Anza College
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Cupertino,_California" title="Cupertino, California">
        Cupertino
       </a>
       , which is also the tenth-highest ranked in the nation. Other relatively well-ranked Bay Area community colleges include
       <a href="/wiki/Foothill_College" title="Foothill College">
        Foothill College
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/City_College_of_San_Francisco" title="City College of San Francisco">
        City College of San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/West_Valley_College" title="West Valley College">
        West Valley College
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Diablo_Valley_College" title="Diablo Valley College">
        Diablo Valley College
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Positas_College" title="Las Positas College">
        Las Positas College
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">
        Primary and secondary schools
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary schools">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_California" title="List of high schools in California">
        List of high schools in California
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Public primary and secondary education in the Bay Area is provided through school districts organized through three structures: elementary school districts, high school districts, or unified school districts, and are governed by an elected board. In addition, many Bay Area counties and the city of San Francisco operate "special service schools" that are geared towards providing education to students with handicaps or
       <a href="/wiki/Special_needs" title="Special needs">
        special needs
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publiceducation_189-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-publiceducation-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An alternative public educational setting is offered by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_schools" title="Charter schools">
        charter schools
       </a>
       , which may be established with a renewable charter of up to five years by third parties. The mechanism for charter schools in the Bay Area is governed by the California Charter Schools Act of 1992.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to rankings compiled by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">
         U.S. News &amp; World Report
        </a>
       </i>
       , the highest-ranked high school in California is the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Collegiate_School" title="Pacific Collegiate School">
        Pacific Collegiate School
       </a>
       , located in
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">
        Santa Cruz
       </a>
       and part of the greater Bay Area. Within the traditional nine-county boundaries, the highest ranked high school is
       <a href="/wiki/KIPP_San_Jose_Collegiate" title="KIPP San Jose Collegiate">
        KIPP San Jose Collegiate
       </a>
       in San Jose. Among the top twenty high schools in California include
       <a href="/wiki/Lowell_High_School_(San_Francisco)" title="Lowell High School (San Francisco)">
        Lowell High School
       </a>
       in San Francisco,
       <a href="/wiki/Monta_Vista_High_School" title="Monta Vista High School">
        Monta Vista High School
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cupertino" title="Cupertino">
        Cupertino
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/University_Preparatory_Academy" title="University Preparatory Academy">
        University Preparatory Academy
       </a>
       in San Jose,
       <a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Jose_High_School" title="Mission San Jose High School">
        Mission San Jose High School
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_California" title="Fremont, California">
        Fremont
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Charter_High_School" title="Oakland Charter High School">
        Oakland Charter High School
       </a>
       in Oakland,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_M._Gunn_High_School" title="Henry M. Gunn High School">
        Henry M. Gunn High School
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">
        Palo Alto
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_High_School_(California)" title="Saratoga High School (California)">
        Saratoga High School
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Saratoga,_California" title="Saratoga, California">
        Saratoga
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_California" title="Climate of California">
        Climate of California
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:254px;max-width:254px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="1270" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg/250px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg/375px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg/500px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skyline_Boulevard" title="Skyline Boulevard">
           Skyline Boulevard
          </a>
          stretches through the Santa Cruz Mountains, here atop
          <a href="/wiki/Portola_Valley,_California" title="Portola Valley, California">
           Portola Valley, California
          </a>
          . During the winter and spring, hills surrounding the San Francisco Bay Area are lush and green.
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="1572" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg/250px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg/375px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg/500px-San_Francisco_Bay_Area_Skyline_Blvd2.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          The same location during the summer months. Because rain is rare in the San Francisco Bay Area during this time, the surrounding hills quickly become dry and golden-hued in grassy areas.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is located in the relatively rare
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate#Warm-summer_Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        warm-summer Mediterranean climate
       </a>
       zone (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen
       </a>
       <i>
        Csb
       </i>
       ) that is a characteristic of California's coast, with moist mild winters and dry summers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ggclimate_192-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ggclimate-192">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is largely influenced by the cold
       <a href="/wiki/California_Current" title="California Current">
        California Current
       </a>
       , which penetrates the natural mountainous barrier along the coast by traveling through various gaps.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOASJ_193-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NOASJ-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In terms of
       <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">
        precipitation
       </a>
       , this means that the Bay Area has pronounced wet and dry seasons. The wet season, which roughly runs between November and March, is the source of about 82% of annual precipitation in the area. In the South Bay and further inland, while the wet season is cool and mild, the summer dry season is characterized by warm sunny days,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOASJ_193-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NOASJ-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while in San Francisco and areas closer to the Golden Gate strait, the dry season is periodically affected by fog.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fog_194-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fog-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to the Bay Area's diverse topography, the result of the clashing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">
        tectonic plates
       </a>
       , the region is home to numerous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microclimates" title="Microclimates">
        microclimates
       </a>
       that lead to pronounced differences in climate and temperature over short distances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ggclimate_192-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ggclimate-192">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG_climate_195-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SFG_climate-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Within the city of San Francisco, natural and artificial topographical features direct the movement of wind and fog, resulting in startlingly varied climates between city blocks. Along the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Strait" title="Golden Gate Strait">
        Golden Gate Strait
       </a>
       , oceanic wind and fog from the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       are able to penetrate the mountain barriers inland into the Bay Area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG_climate_195-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-SFG_climate-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the summer, rising hot air in California's interior valleys creates a low pressure area that draws winds from the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Pacific_High" title="North Pacific High">
        North Pacific High
       </a>
       through the Golden Gate, which creates the city's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_fog_generation" title="San Francisco fog generation">
        characteristic cool winds and fog
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fog_194-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-fog-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The microclimate phenomenon is most pronounced during this time, when fog penetration is at its maximum in areas near the Golden Gate strait,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG_climate_195-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-SFG_climate-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while the South Bay and areas further inland are sunny and dry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOASJ_193-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-NOASJ-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Along the San Francisco peninsula, gaps in the
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Mountains" title="Santa Cruz Mountains">
        Santa Cruz Mountains
       </a>
       , one south of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Bruno_Mountain" title="San Bruno Mountain">
        San Bruno Mountain
       </a>
       and another in Crystal Springs, allow oceanic weather into the interior and causing a cooling effect for cities along the Peninsula and even as far south as San Jose. This weather pattern is also the source for delays at
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_International_Airport" title="San Francisco International Airport">
        San Francisco International Airport
       </a>
       . In Marin county north of the Golden Gate strait, two gaps north of
       <a href="/wiki/Muir_Woods_National_Monument" title="Muir Woods National Monument">
        Muir Woods
       </a>
       bring cold air across the
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_Headlands" title="Marin Headlands">
        Marin Headlands
       </a>
       , with the cooling affect reaching as far north as
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa,_California" title="Santa Rosa, California">
        Santa Rosa
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG_climate_195-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-SFG_climate-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Further inland, the East Bay receives oceanic weather that travels through the Golden Gate strait, and further diffuses that air through the
       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Hills" title="Berkeley Hills">
        Berkeley Hills
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Niles_Canyon" title="Niles Canyon">
        Niles Canyon
       </a>
       and the Hayward Pass into the
       <a href="/wiki/Livermore_Valley" title="Livermore Valley">
        Livermore Valley
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Pass" title="Altamont Pass">
        Altamont Pass
       </a>
       . Here, the resulting breeze is so strong that it is home to one of the world's largest array of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_turbines" title="Wind turbines">
        wind turbines
       </a>
       . Further north, the
       <a href="/wiki/Carquinez_Strait" title="Carquinez Strait">
        Carquinez Strait
       </a>
       funnels the ocean weather into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_River_Delta" title="San Joaquin River Delta">
        San Joaquin River Delta
       </a>
       , causing a cooling effect in
       <a href="/wiki/Stockton,_California" title="Stockton, California">
        Stockton
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">
        Sacramento
       </a>
       , so that these cities are also cooler than their
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Valley_(California)" title="Central Valley (California)">
        Central Valley
       </a>
       counterparts in the south.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFG_climate_195-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-SFG_climate-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
