      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Ecology_of_the_San_Francisco_Estuary" title="Ecology of the San Francisco Estuary">
        Ecology of the San Francisco Estuary
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_species_endemic_to_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="List of species endemic to the San Francisco Bay Area">
        List of species endemic to the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_wildlife">
        Marine wildlife
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Marine wildlife">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29,_2010.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of river otter sunning on rocks." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg/250px-River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg/375px-River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg/500px-River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29%2C_2010.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:River_otter_Richmond_Marina_Scott_Campbell_July_29,_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         River otter sunning on rocks in the
         <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
          Richmond Marina
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of a California golden beaver." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="1944" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg/250px-Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg/375px-Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg/500px-Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beaver_Yearling_Grooming_Alhambra_Creek_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A California golden beaver in
         <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Creek" title="Alhambra Creek">
          Alhambra Creek
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Martinez,_California" title="Martinez, California">
          Martinez
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is home to a diverse array of wildlife and, along with the connected
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_River_Delta" title="San Joaquin River Delta">
        San Joaquin River Delta
       </a>
       represents one of California's most important ecological habitats.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       California's
       <a href="/wiki/Dungeness_crab" title="Dungeness crab">
        Dungeness crab
       </a>
       , Pacific
       <a href="/wiki/Halibut" title="Halibut">
        halibut
       </a>
       , and the California
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scorpionfish" title="Scorpionfish">
        scorpionfish
       </a>
       are all significant components of the bay's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fisheries" title="Fisheries">
        fisheries
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The bay's
       <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">
        salt marshes
       </a>
       now represent most of California's remaining salt marsh and support a number of endangered
       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">
        species
       </a>
       and provide key ecosystem services such as filtering pollutants and
       <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">
        sediments
       </a>
       from the rivers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most famously, the bay is a key link in the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Flyway" title="Pacific Flyway">
        Pacific Flyway
       </a>
       and with millions of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shorebirds" title="Shorebirds">
        shorebirds
       </a>
       annually visiting the bay shallows as a refuge, is the most important component of the flyway south of
       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
        Alaska
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many
       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">
        endangered species
       </a>
       of birds are also found here: the
       <a href="/wiki/California_least_tern" title="California least tern">
        California least tern
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_clapper_rail" title="California clapper rail">
        California clapper rail
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Snowy_egret" title="Snowy egret">
        snowy egret
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_crowned_night_heron" title="Black crowned night heron">
        black crowned night heron
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also a significant diversity of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salmonids" title="Salmonids">
        salmonids
       </a>
       present in the bay.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steelhead" title="Steelhead">
        Steelhead
       </a>
       populations in California have dramatically declined due to human and natural causes; in the Bay Area, all naturally spawned
       <a href="/wiki/Fish_migration" title="Fish migration">
        anadromous
       </a>
       steelhead populations below natural and manmade impassable barriers in California streams from the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_River_(California)" title="Russian River (California)">
        Russian River
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Aptos_Creek" title="Aptos Creek">
        Aptos Creek
       </a>
       , and the drainages of San Francisco, San Pablo, and Suisun Bays are listed as threatened under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act" title="Endangered Species Act">
        Federal Endangered Species Act
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
        <a href="#cite_note-206">
         [206]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Central California Coast
       <a href="/wiki/Coho_salmon" title="Coho salmon">
        coho salmon
       </a>
       population is the most endangered of the many troubled salmon populations on the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">
        west coast of the United States
       </a>
       , including populations residing in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tributaries" title="Tributaries">
        tributaries
       </a>
       to the San Francisco Bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Science_207-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Science-207">
         [207]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Industrial, mining, and other uses of
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">
        mercury
       </a>
       have resulted in a widespread distribution of that poisonous metal in the bay, with uptake in the bay's
       <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">
        phytoplankton
       </a>
       and contamination of its
       <a href="/wiki/Game_fish" title="Game fish">
        sportfish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
        <a href="#cite_note-208">
         [208]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aquatic mammals are also present in the bay. Before 1825, Spanish, French, English, Russians and Americans were drawn to the Bay Area to harvest prodigious quantities of
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_beaver" title="North American beaver">
        beaver
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_river_otter" title="North American river otter">
        river otter
       </a>
       , marten, fisher, mink, fox, weasel, harbor and
       <a href="/wiki/Fur_seal" title="Fur seal">
        fur seals
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_otter" title="Sea otter">
        sea otter
       </a>
       . This early fur trade, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Fur_Rush" title="California Fur Rush">
        California Fur Rush
       </a>
       , was more than any other single factor, responsible for opening up the West and the San Francisco Bay Area, in particular, to world trade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skinner_209-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Skinner-209">
         [209]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1817 sea otter in the area were practically eliminated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
        <a href="#cite_note-210">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since then, the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_beaver" title="North American beaver">
        California golden beaver
       </a>
       has re-established a presence in the
       <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Creek" title="Alhambra Creek">
        Alhambra Creek
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
        <a href="#cite_note-211">
         [211]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_river_otter" title="North American river otter">
        North American river otter
       </a>
       which was first reported in
       <a href="/wiki/Redwood_Creek_(Marin_County)" title="Redwood Creek (Marin County)">
        Redwood Creek
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Muir_Beach,_California" title="Muir Beach, California">
        Muir Beach
       </a>
       in 1996,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
        <a href="#cite_note-212">
         [212]
        </a>
       </sup>
       has since been spotted in the North Bay's
       <a href="/wiki/Corte_Madera_Creek_(Marin_County,_California)" title="Corte Madera Creek (Marin County, California)">
        Corte Madera Creek
       </a>
       , the South Bay's
       <a href="/wiki/Coyote_Creek_(Santa_Clara_County)" title="Coyote Creek (Santa Clara County)">
        Coyote Creek
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
        <a href="#cite_note-213">
         [213]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as in 2010 in San Francisco Bay itself at the
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">
        Richmond Marina
       </a>
       . Other mammals include the internationally famous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_lions" title="Sea lions">
        sea lions
       </a>
       who began inhabiting San Francisco's
       <a href="/wiki/Pier_39" title="Pier 39">
        Pier 39
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">
        1989 Loma Prieta earthquake
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
        <a href="#cite_note-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the locally famous
       <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_the_Whale" title="Humphrey the Whale">
        Humphrey the Whale
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">
        humpback whale
       </a>
       who entered San Francisco Bay twice on errant migrations in the late 1980s and early 1990s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
        <a href="#cite_note-215">
         [215]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">
        Bottlenose dolphins
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">
        harbor porpoises
       </a>
       have recently returned to the bay, having been absent for many decades. Historically, this was the northern extent of their warm-water species range.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
        <a href="#cite_note-216">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Birds">
        Birds
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Birds">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg">
         <img alt="An image of a family of burrowing owls inside their holes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="809" data-file-width="1046" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg/250px-Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg/375px-Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg/500px-Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burrowing_Owl_Family_in_Antioch.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A family of owls turned out of their homes in
         <a href="/wiki/Antioch,_California" title="Antioch, California">
          Antioch
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In addition to the many species of marine birds that can be seen in the Bay Area, many other species of birds make the Bay Area their home, making the region a popular destination for
       <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">
        birdwatching
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
        <a href="#cite_note-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many birds, including many described in the following paragraphs, are listed as
       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">
        endangered species
       </a>
       despite once being common in the region, due to human and other impacts.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Burrowing_owl" title="Burrowing owl">
        Western burrowing owls
       </a>
       were originally listed as a
       <a href="/wiki/California_species_of_special_concern" title="California species of special concern">
        species of special concern
       </a>
       by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Department_of_Fish_and_Game" title="California Department of Fish and Game">
        California Department of Fish and Game
       </a>
       in 1979. California's population declined 60% from the 1980s to the early 1990s, and continues to decline at roughly 8% per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
        <a href="#cite_note-218">
         [218]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 1992–93 survey reported little to no breeding burrowing owls in most of the western counties in the Bay Area, leaving only
       <a href="/wiki/Alameda_County,_California" title="Alameda County, California">
        Alameda
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contra_Costa_County" title="Contra Costa County">
        Contra Costa
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solano_County" title="Solano County">
        Solano
       </a>
       counties as remnants of a once large breeding range.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         [219]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bald_eagles" title="Bald eagles">
        Bald eagles
       </a>
       were once common in the Bay Area, but habitat destruction and thinning of eggs from
       <a href="/wiki/DDT" title="DDT">
        DDT
       </a>
       poisoning reduced the California state population to 35 nesting pairs. Bald eagles disappeared from the Bay Area in 1915, and only began returning in recent years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baldeagle_220-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-baldeagle-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1980s an effort to re-introduce the species to the area began with the Santa Cruz Predatory Bird Research Group and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Zoo" title="San Francisco Zoo">
        San Francisco Zoo
       </a>
       importing birds and eggs from
       <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">
        Vancouver Island
       </a>
       and northeastern California,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
        <a href="#cite_note-221">
         [221]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and there are now nineteen nesting couples in eight of the Bay Area's nine counties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baldeagle_220-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-baldeagle-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other once absent species that have returned to the Bay Area include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swainson%E2%80%99s_hawk" title="Swainson’s hawk">
        Swainson’s hawk
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_tailed_kite" title="White tailed kite">
        white tailed kite
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Osprey" title="Osprey">
        osprey
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baldeagle_220-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-baldeagle-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1927, zoologist
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Grinnell" title="Joseph Grinnell">
        Joseph Grinnell
       </a>
       wrote that osprey were only rare visitors to the San Francisco Bay Area, although he noted records of one or two used nests in the broken tops of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coast_redwood" title="Coast redwood">
        redwood
       </a>
       trees along the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_River_(California)" title="Russian River (California)">
        Russian River
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
        <a href="#cite_note-222">
         [222]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1989, the southern breeding range of the osprey in the Bay Area was
       <a href="/wiki/Kent_Lake" title="Kent Lake">
        Kent Lake
       </a>
       , although osprey were noted to be extending their range further south in the Central Valley and the Sierra Nevada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
        <a href="#cite_note-223">
         [223]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2014, a Bay Area-wide survey found osprey had extended their breeding range southward with nesting sites as far south as
       <a href="/wiki/Bayview-Hunters_Point,_San_Francisco" title="Bayview-Hunters Point, San Francisco">
        Hunters Point
       </a>
       in San Francisco on the west side and
       <a href="/wiki/Hayward,_California" title="Hayward, California">
        Hayward
       </a>
       on the east side, while further studies have found nesting sites as far south as the
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Gatos_Creek_(Santa_Clara_County,_California)" title="Los Gatos Creek (Santa Clara County, California)">
        Los Gatos Creek
       </a>
       watershed, indicating that the nesting range now includes the entire length of San Francisco Bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bousman2007_224-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bousman2007-224">
         [224]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most nests were built on man-made structures close to areas of human disturbance, likely due to lack of mature trees near the Bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
        <a href="#cite_note-225">
         [225]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_turkey" title="Wild turkey">
        wild turkey
       </a>
       population was introduced in the 1960s by state game officials, and by 2015 have become a common sight in East Bay communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rub_226-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rub-226">
         [226]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_landforms">
        Geology and landforms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Geology and landforms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BayareaUSGS.jpg">
         <img alt="A satellite image of the Bay Area, depicting features visible from space." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="798" data-file-width="769" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BayareaUSGS.jpg/220px-BayareaUSGS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BayareaUSGS.jpg/330px-BayareaUSGS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BayareaUSGS.jpg/440px-BayareaUSGS.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BayareaUSGS.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USGS" title="USGS">
          USGS
         </a>
         satellite photo of the Bay Area taken in 1999. The gray areas are signs of
         <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">
          urbanization
         </a>
         and represent the most populated areas.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is well known for the complexity of its landforms that are the result of millions of years by the forces of
       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">
        plate tectonics
       </a>
       , since the region is located in the middle of a meeting point between two plates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
        <a href="#cite_note-227">
         [227]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nine out of eleven distinct
       <i>
        assemblages
       </i>
       have been identified in a single county, Alameda.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
        <a href="#cite_note-228">
         [228]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Diverse assemblages adjoin in complex arrangements due to offsets along the many faults (both active and stable) in the area. As a consequence, many types of rock and soil are found in the region. The oldest rocks are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rocks" title="Metamorphic rocks">
        metamorphic rocks
       </a>
       that are associated with granite in the
       <a href="/wiki/Salinian_Block" title="Salinian Block">
        Salinian Block
       </a>
       west of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Andreas_fault" title="San Andreas fault">
        San Andreas fault
       </a>
       . These were formed from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sedimentary" title="Sedimentary">
        sedimentary
       </a>
       rocks of
       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">
        sandstone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        limestone
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">
        shale
       </a>
       in uplifted seabeds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
        <a href="#cite_note-229">
         [229]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Volcanic deposits also exist in the Bay Area, left behind by the movement of the San Andreas fault, whose movement sliced a subduction plate and allowed magma to briefly flow to the surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
        <a href="#cite_note-230">
         [230]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eq-prob.jpg">
         <img alt="A map tracing all the fault lines in the Bay Area, and listing probabilities of earthquakes occurring on them." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="716" data-file-width="535" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Eq-prob.jpg/220px-Eq-prob.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Eq-prob.jpg/330px-Eq-prob.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Eq-prob.jpg/440px-Eq-prob.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eq-prob.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map displaying each of the seven major fault lines in the Bay Area, and the probability of an
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnitude_(earthquake)" title="Magnitude (earthquake)">
          M6.7
         </a>
         earthquake or higher occurring on each fault line between 2003 and 2032.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The region has considerable vertical relief in its landscapes that are not in the
       <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">
        alluvial plains
       </a>
       leading to the bay or in inland valleys. The topography, and geologic history, of the Bay Area can largely be attributed to the compressive forces between the Pacific Plate and the North American plate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
        <a href="#cite_note-231">
         [231]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The three major ridge structures in the Bay Area, part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Range" title="Pacific Coast Range">
        Pacific Coast Range
       </a>
       , are all roughly parallel to the major
       <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">
        faults
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Mountains" title="Santa Cruz Mountains">
        Santa Cruz Mountains
       </a>
       along the San Francisco Peninsula and the
       <a href="/wiki/Marin_Hills" title="Marin Hills">
        Marin Hills
       </a>
       in Marin County follow the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Andreas_Fault" title="San Andreas Fault">
        San Andreas fault
       </a>
       , The
       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Hills" title="Berkeley Hills">
        Berkeley Hills
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Leandro_Hills" title="San Leandro Hills">
        San Leandro Hills
       </a>
       and their southern ridgeline extension through
       <a href="/wiki/Mission_Peak" title="Mission Peak">
        Mission Peak
       </a>
       roughly follow the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hayward_Fault" title="Hayward Fault">
        Hayward fault
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Diablo_Range" title="Diablo Range">
        Diablo Range
       </a>
       , which includes
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Diablo" title="Mount Diablo">
        Mount Diablo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Hamilton_(California)" title="Mount Hamilton (California)">
        Mount Hamilton
       </a>
       and runs along the
       <a href="/wiki/Calaveras_Fault" title="Calaveras Fault">
        Calaveras fault
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
        <a href="#cite_note-232">
         [232]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In total, the Bay Area is traversed by seven major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earthquake_fault" title="Earthquake fault">
        fault
       </a>
       systems with hundreds of related faults, all of which are stressed by the relative motion between the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">
        Pacific Plate
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">
        North American Plate
       </a>
       or by compressive stresses between these plates. The fault systems include the
       <a href="/wiki/Hayward_Fault_Zone" title="Hayward Fault Zone">
        Hayward Fault Zone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Concord_Fault" title="Concord Fault">
        Concord-Green Valley Fault
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Calaveras_Fault" title="Calaveras Fault">
        Calaveras Fault
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Clayton-Marsh_Creek-Greenville_Fault" title="Clayton-Marsh Creek-Greenville Fault">
        Clayton-Marsh Creek-Greenville Fault
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rodgers_Creek_Fault" title="Rodgers Creek Fault">
        Rodgers Creek Fault
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Gregorio_Fault" title="San Gregorio Fault">
        San Gregorio Fault
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
        <a href="#cite_note-233">
         [233]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Significant blind
       <a href="/wiki/Thrust_fault" title="Thrust fault">
        thrust faults
       </a>
       (faults with near vertical motion and no surface ruptures) are associated with portions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Mountains" title="Santa Cruz Mountains">
        Santa Cruz Mountains
       </a>
       and the northern reaches of the
       <a href="/wiki/Diablo_Range" title="Diablo Range">
        Diablo Range
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Diablo" title="Mount Diablo">
        Mount Diablo
       </a>
       . These "hidden" faults, which are not as well known, pose a significant earthquake hazard.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
        <a href="#cite_note-234">
         [234]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Among the more well-understood faults, scientists estimate a 63% probability of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earthquake_magnitude" title="Earthquake magnitude">
        magnitude
       </a>
       6.7 earthquake occurring along either the Hayward, Rogers Creek, or San Andreas fault, with an earthquake more likely to occur in the East Bay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
        <a href="#cite_note-235">
         [235]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two of the largest earthquakes in recent history were the
       <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">
        1906 San Francisco earthquake
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">
        1989 Loma Prieta earthquake
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">
        Hydrography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Hydrography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrography_of_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Hydrography of the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Hydrography of the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sfestuaryhistorical.gif">
         <img alt="A map of all the water features in the Bay Area." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="559" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Sfestuaryhistorical.gif/220px-Sfestuaryhistorical.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Sfestuaryhistorical.gif/330px-Sfestuaryhistorical.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Sfestuaryhistorical.gif/440px-Sfestuaryhistorical.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sfestuaryhistorical.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of the water features in the San Francisco Bay Area, including the bay and adjacent
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshes" title="Marshes">
          marshes
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Pond" title="Pond">
          ponds
         </a>
         , and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tributaries" title="Tributaries">
          tributaries
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bay Area is home to a complex network of watersheds, marshes, rivers, creeks, reservoirs, and bays that predominantly drain into the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco Bay
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . The largest bodies of water in the Bay Area are the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Bay" title="San Pablo Bay">
        San Pablo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Suisun_Bay" title="Suisun Bay">
        Suisun
       </a>
       estuaries. Major rivers of the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Bay_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="North Bay (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        North Bay
       </a>
       include the
       <a href="/wiki/Napa_River" title="Napa River">
        Napa River
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Petaluma_River" title="Petaluma River">
        Petaluma River
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Gualala_River" title="Gualala River">
        Gualala River
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_River_(California)" title="Russian River (California)">
        Russian River
       </a>
       ; the former two drain into
       <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Bay" title="San Pablo Bay">
        San Pablo Bay
       </a>
       , the latter two into the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . In the
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_Valley" title="Santa Clara Valley">
        South Bay
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalupe_River_(California)" title="Guadalupe River (California)">
        Guadalupe River
       </a>
       drains into
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">
        San Francisco Bay
       </a>
       near
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alviso,_San_Jose,_California" title="Alviso, San Jose, California">
        Alviso
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
        <a href="#cite_note-236">
         [236]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also several lakes present in the Bay Area, including man-made lakes like
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Berryessa" title="Lake Berryessa">
        Lake Berryessa
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
        <a href="#cite_note-237">
         [237]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and natural albeit heavily modified lakes like
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Merritt" title="Lake Merritt">
        Lake Merritt
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
        <a href="#cite_note-238">
         [238]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the introduction of European agricultural methods, the shores of San Francisco Bay consisted mostly of tidal marshes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marshes_239-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-marshes-239">
         [239]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today, the bay has been significantly altered heavily re-engineered to accommodate the needs of water delivery, shipping, agriculture, and urban development, with side effects including the loss of wetlands and the introduction of contaminants and
       <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">
        invasive species
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
        <a href="#cite_note-240">
         [240]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 85% of those marshes have been lost or destroyed, but about 50 marshes and marsh fragments remain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marshes_239-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-marshes-239">
         [239]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Huge tracts of the marshes were originally destroyed by farmers for agricultural purposes, then repurposed to serve as
       <a href="/wiki/Salt_evaporation_pond" title="Salt evaporation pond">
        salt evaporation ponds
       </a>
       to produce salt for food and other purposes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
        <a href="#cite_note-241">
         [241]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today, regulations limit the destruction of tidal marshes, and large portions are currently being rehabilitated to its natural state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marshes_239-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-marshes-239">
         [239]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Government and politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Politics in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Politics in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SFCityHall.png">
         <img alt="An image of the San Francisco City Hall." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1001" data-file-width="1538" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SFCityHall.png/220px-SFCityHall.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SFCityHall.png/330px-SFCityHall.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SFCityHall.png/440px-SFCityHall.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SFCityHall.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The consolidated city-county government of
         <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">
          San Francisco
         </a>
         manages its many responsibilities inside the
         <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_City_Hall" title="San Francisco City Hall">
          San Francisco City Hall building
         </a>
         . In addition to city and county governments, a variety of agencies and districts are also involved in the governance of the Bay Area.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Government in the San Francisco Bay Area consists of multiple actors, including 101 city and nine county governments, a dozen regional agencies, and a large number of single-purpose
       <a href="/wiki/Special_district_(United_States)" title="Special district (United States)">
        special districts
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Municipal_utility_district" title="Municipal utility district">
        municipal utility districts
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Transit_district" title="Transit district">
        transit districts
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
        <a href="#cite_note-242">
         [242]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Incorporated cities are responsible for providing police service, zoning, issuing building permits, and maintaining public streets among other duties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
        <a href="#cite_note-243">
         [243]
        </a>
       </sup>
       County governments are responsible for elections and voter registration, vital records, property assessment and records, tax collection, public health, agricultural regulations, and building inspections, among other duties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
        <a href="#cite_note-244">
         [244]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
        <a href="#cite_note-245">
         [245]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Public education is provided by independent school districts, which may be organized as elementary districts, high school districts, unified school districts combining elementary and high school grades, or community college districts, and are managed by an elected school board.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publiceducation_189-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-publiceducation-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A variety of special districts also exist and provide a single purpose, such as delivering public transit in the case of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Rapid_Transit_District" title="Bay Area Rapid Transit District">
        Bay Area Rapid Transit District
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
        <a href="#cite_note-246">
         [246]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or monitoring air quality levels in the case of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Air_Quality_Management_District" title="Bay Area Air Quality Management District">
        Bay Area Air Quality Management District
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutbaaqmd_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aboutbaaqmd-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Politics in the Bay Area is widely regarded as one of the most
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">
        liberal
       </a>
       |liberal]] in
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       and in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
        <a href="#cite_note-247">
         [247]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
        <a href="#cite_note-248">
         [248]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the late 1960s, the Bay Area cemented its role as the most liberal region in California politics, supporting the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_left" title="Center left">
        center left
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic Party
       </a>
       's candidates for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._President" title="U.S. President">
        U.S. President
       </a>
       and continued to support Democratic candidates more than other regions of the state, even as California trended towards the Democratic Party over time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PPIC_249-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PPIC-249">
         [249]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to research by the
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Policy_Institute_of_California" title="Public Policy Institute of California">
        Public Policy Institute of California
       </a>
       , the Bay Area and the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Coast_(California)" title="North Coast (California)">
        North Coast
       </a>
       counties of
       <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_County,_California" title="Humboldt County, California">
        Humboldt
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mendocino_County,_California" title="Mendocino County, California">
        Mendocino
       </a>
       were the most consistently and strongly liberal areas in California.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PPIC_249-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PPIC-249">
         [249]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Secretary_of_State" title="California Secretary of State">
        California Secretary of State
       </a>
       , the Democratic Party holds a voter registration advantage in every
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_congressional_districts" title="California's congressional districts">
        congressional district
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate_districts" title="California State Senate districts">
        state senate district
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly_districts" title="California State Assembly districts">
        state assembly district
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/State_Board_of_Equalization_(California)#Equalization_districts" title="State Board of Equalization (California)">
        State Board of Equalization district
       </a>
       , all nine counties, and all but three of the 101 incorporated municipalities in the Bay Area. On the other hand, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_right" title="Center right">
        center right
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
        Republican Party
       </a>
       holds a voter registration advantage in only one state assembly subdistrict (the portion of
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_4th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 4th State Assembly district">
        California's 4th State Assembly district
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Solano_County,_California" title="Solano County, California">
        Solano county
       </a>
       ) and three cities,
       <a href="/wiki/Atherton,_California" title="Atherton, California">
        Atherton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_California" title="Hillsborough, California">
        Hillsborough
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Danville,_California" title="Danville, California">
        Danville
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
        <a href="#cite_note-250">
         [250]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cook_Partisan_Voting_Index" title="Cook Partisan Voting Index">
        Cook Partisan Voting Index
       </a>
       (CPVI),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congressional_districts" title="Congressional districts">
        congressional districts
       </a>
       the Bay Area tends to favor Democratic candidates by roughly 40 to 50 percentage points, considerably above the mean for California and the nation overall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251">
        <a href="#cite_note-251">
         [251]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed sortable" style="width: 100%;">

        </td>
        <td>
         0.4%
        </td>
        <td>
         22.0%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_County,_California" title="Sonoma County, California">
          Sonoma
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         478,551
        </td>
        <td>
         54.7%
        </td>
        <td>
         51.5%
        </td>
        <td>
         21.6%
        </td>
        <td>
         <span style="color: #2b00d6;">
          <b>
           +29.9%
          </b>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         2.5%
        </td>
        <td>
         1.8%
        </td>
        <td>
         0.7%
        </td>
        <td>
         0.3%
        </td>
        <td>
         0.0%
        </td>
        <td>
         0.3%
        </td>
        <td>
         21.3%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Presidential_elections" title="U.S. Presidential elections">
        U.S. Presidential elections
       </a>
       , the nine-county Bay Area voted for
       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
        Republican
       </a>
       candidates in the last four decades only three times, in all three cases voting for a Californian: in 1972 for
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
        Richard Nixon
       </a>
       and again in
       <a href="/wiki/Category:1980_in_politics" title="Category:1980 in politics">
        1980
       </a>
       and in 1984 for
       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">
        Ronald Reagan
       </a>
       . The last county to vote for a Republican Presidential candidate was
       <a href="/wiki/Napa_County,_California" title="Napa County, California">
        Napa county
       </a>
       in 1988 for
       <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">
        George H. W. Bush
       </a>
       . Since then, all nine Bay Area counties have voted consistently for the Democratic candidate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254">
        <a href="#cite_note-254">
         [254]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Currently, both of California's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senators" title="U.S. Senators">
        U.S. Senators
       </a>
       are Democrats, and all twelve
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts" title="List of United States congressional districts">
        U.S. congressional districts
       </a>
       located wholly or partially in the Bay Area are represented by a Democratic representative. Additionally, every Bay Area member of the
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate" title="California State Senate">
        California State Senate
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly" title="California State Assembly">
        California State Assembly
       </a>
       is a registered Democrat, except for
       <a href="/wiki/Catharine_Baker" title="Catharine Baker">
        Catharine Baker
       </a>
       , who represents
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_16th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 16th State Assembly district">
        California's 16th State Assembly district
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255">
        <a href="#cite_note-255">
         [255]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The association between the Bay Area and progressive politics has led the term "San Francisco values" being used by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative" title="Conservative">
        conservative
       </a>
       commentators in a pejorative sense to describe the secular progressive culture in the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threedirtywords_256-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-threedirtywords-256">
         [256]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Francisco_Bay_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_the_San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="Transportation in the San Francisco Bay Area">
        Transportation in the San Francisco Bay Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg">
         <img alt="A transit map with lines depicting routes operated by various public rail agencies in the Bay Area." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1761" data-file-width="2362" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg/300px-SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg/450px-SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg/600px-SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SF_Bay_Rail_Transit.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Bay Area is served by a variety of rail transit systems, with services provided by
         <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Corridor_Express" title="Altamont Corridor Express">
          ACE
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
          Amtrak
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Bay Area Rapid Transit">
          BART
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Caltrain" title="Caltrain">
          Caltrain
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Muni_Metro" title="Muni Metro">
          Muni Metro
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonoma_Marin_Area_Rail_Transit" title="Sonoma Marin Area Rail Transit">
          SMART
         </a>
         , and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valley_Transportation_Authority" title="Valley Transportation Authority">
          VTA
         </a>
         displayed here.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Transportation in the San Francisco Bay Area is reliant on a complex multimodal infrastructure consisting of roads, bridges, highways, rail, tunnels, airports, and bike and pedestrian paths. The development, maintenance, and operation of these different modes of transportation are overseen by various agencies, including the California Department of Transportation (Caltrans),
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Municipal_Transportation_Agency" title="San Francisco Municipal Transportation Agency">
        San Francisco Municipal Transportation Agency
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transportation_Commission_(San_Francisco_Bay_Area)" title="Metropolitan Transportation Commission (San Francisco Bay Area)">
        Metropolitan Transportation Commission
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257">
        <a href="#cite_note-257">
         [257]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These and other organizations collectively manage several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_highway" title="Interstate highway">
        interstate highways
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/State_highways_in_California" title="State highways in California">
        state routes
       </a>
       , two
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
        subway
       </a>
       networks, two
       <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">
        commuter rail
       </a>
       agencies, eight trans-bay bridges, transbay ferry service, local
       <a href="/wiki/Transit_bus" title="Transit bus">
        bus
       </a>
       service,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seamlesstransit_258-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-seamlesstransit-258">
         [258]
        </a>
       </sup>
       three
       <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">
        international airports
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_International_Airport" title="San Francisco International Airport">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_International_Airport" title="San Jose International Airport">
        San Jose
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_International_Airport" title="Oakland International Airport">
        Oakland
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
        <a href="#cite_note-259">
         [259]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and an extensive network of roads, tunnels, and paths such as the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Trail" title="San Francisco Bay Trail">
        San Francisco Bay Trail
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
        <a href="#cite_note-260">
         [260]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bay Area hosts an extensive freeway and highway system that is particularly prone to
       <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">
        traffic congestion
       </a>
       , with one study by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inrix" title="Inrix">
        Inrix
       </a>
       concluding that the Bay Area's traffic was the fourth worst in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
        <a href="#cite_note-261">
         [261]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are some city streets in San Francisco where gaps occur in the freeway system, partly the result of the
       <a href="/wiki/Highway_revolts_in_the_United_States#San_Francisco" title="Highway revolts in the United States">
        Freeway Revolt
       </a>
       , which prevented a freeway-only thoroughfare through San Francisco between the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge">
        San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge
       </a>
       , the western terminus of
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80_in_California" title="Interstate 80 in California">
        Interstate 80
       </a>
       , and the southern terminus of the Golden Gate Bridge (
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_101_in_California" title="U.S. Route 101 in California">
        U.S. Route 101
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262">
        <a href="#cite_note-262">
         [262]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additional damage that occurred in the wake of the 1989
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="Loma Prieta earthquake">
        Loma Prieta earthquake
       </a>
       resulted in freeway segments being removed instead of being reinforced or rebuilt, leading to the revitalization of neighborhoods such as San Francisco's
       <a href="/wiki/Embarcadero_(San_Francisco)" title="Embarcadero (San Francisco)">
        Embarcadero
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
        <a href="#cite_note-263">
         [263]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The greater Bay Area contains the three principal north-south highways in California:
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">
        Interstate 5
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_101" title="U.S. Route 101">
        U.S. Route 101
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_1" title="California State Route 1">
        California State Route 1
       </a>
       . U.S. 101 and State Route 1 directly serve the traditional nine-county region, while Interstate 5 bypasses to the east in San Joaquin County to provide a more direct
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
        Los Angeles
       </a>
       –
       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">
        Sacramento
       </a>
       route. Additional local highways connect the various subregions of the Bay Area together.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catg_264-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-catg-264">
         [264]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are over two dozen
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transit" title="Public transit">
        public transit
       </a>
       agencies in the Bay Area with overlapping service areas that utilize different
       <a href="/wiki/Mode_of_transport" title="Mode of transport">
        modes
       </a>
       , with designated connection points between the various operators.
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Bay Area Rapid Transit">
        Bay Area Rapid Transit
       </a>
       (BART), a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_rail" title="Heavy rail">
        heavy rail
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
        metro
       </a>
       system, operates in four counties and connects San Francisco and Oakland via an underwater tube. Other
       <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">
        commuter rail
       </a>
       systems link San Francisco with the Peninsula and San Jose (
       <a href="/wiki/Caltrain" title="Caltrain">
        Caltrain
       </a>
       ), San Jose with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tri-Valley_Area" title="Tri-Valley Area">
        Tri-Valley Area
       </a>
       and San Joaquin county (
       <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Corridor_Express" title="Altamont Corridor Express">
        ACE
       </a>
       ), and Sonoma with Marin county (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonoma_Marin_Area_Rail_Transit" title="Sonoma Marin Area Rail Transit">
        SMART
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seamlesstransit_258-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-seamlesstransit-258">
         [258]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition,
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       provides frequent commuter service between and San Jose and the East Bay with
       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">
        Sacramento
       </a>
       , and long distance service to other parts of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265">
        <a href="#cite_note-265">
         [265]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Muni_Metro" title="Muni Metro">
        Muni Metro
       </a>
       operates a hybrid
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar">
        streetcar
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
        subway
       </a>
       system within the city of San Francisco, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valley_Transportation_Authority" title="Valley Transportation Authority">
        VTA
       </a>
       operates a
       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">
        light rail
       </a>
       system in Santa Clara county. These rail systems are supplemented by numerous bus agencies and transbay
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferries" title="Ferries">
        ferries
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Ferry" title="Golden Gate Ferry">
        Golden Gate Ferry
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Water_Transit_Authority" title="San Francisco Bay Water Transit Authority">
        San Francisco Bay Water Transit Authority
       </a>
       . Most of these agencies accept the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clipper_Card" title="Clipper Card">
        Clipper Card
       </a>
       , a reloadable
       <a href="/wiki/Contactless_smart_card" title="Contactless smart card">
        contactless smart card
       </a>
       , as a universal electronic payment system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seamlesstransit_258-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-seamlesstransit-258">
         [258]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
        See also
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>

          <cite class="citation news">
           Torres, Blanca (2017-04-28).
           <a class="external text" href="https://www.bizjournals.com/sanfrancisco/news/2017/04/28/san-francisco-seattle-housing-production-pipelines.html" rel="nofollow">
            "Housing's tale of two cities: Seattle builds, S.F. lags"
           </a>
           . San Francisco Business Times.
           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170502005754/https://www.bizjournals.com/sanfrancisco/news/2017/04/28/san-francisco-seattle-housing-production-pipelines.html" rel="nofollow">
            Archived
           </a>
           from the original on 2017-05-02
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             2017-12-04
            </span>
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            So how can smaller Seattle make so much more housing happen than San Francisco? Developers active in both cities and officials who have worked in both point to structural differences that outweigh the demographic similarities. In San Francisco, development issues are routinely subject to consideration by neighborhood bodies, approval by the city planning commission and often ratification by its board of supervisors, with opportunities for decisions to be appealed. Seattle’s approval process is much more streamlined...The city’s planning commission is strictly a policy entity. It does not approve or reject projects. The city council weighs in on projects only in rare cases. [In S.F.]...he thinks that the California Environmental Quality Act, known as CEQA, makes it too easy for residents to sue projects, effectively holding them up for years or blocking them.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Housing%E2%80%99s+tale+of+two+cities%3A+Seattle+builds%2C+S.F.+lags&amp;rft.date=2017-04-28&amp;rft.aulast=Torres&amp;rft.aufirst=Blanca&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bizjournals.com%2Fsanfrancisco%2Fnews%2F2017%2F04%2F28%2Fsan-francisco-seattle-housing-production-pipelines.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASan+Francisco+Bay+Area">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-homes_where_the_jobs_are-172">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-homes_where_the_jobs_are_172-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation news">
           Clark, Patrick (2017-06-23).
           <a class="external text" href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2017-06-23/why-can-t-they-build-more-homes-where-the-jobs-are" rel="nofollow">
            "Why Can't They Build More Homes Where the Jobs Are?"
           </a>
           . Bloomberg.
           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170828201133/https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2017-06-23/why-can-t-they-build-more-homes-where-the-jobs-are" rel="nofollow">
            Archived
           </a>
           from the original on 2017-08-28
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             2017-12-01
            </span>
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            San Francisco's metropolitan area added 373,000 net new jobs in the last five years—but issued permits for only 58,000 units of new housing. The lack of new construction has exacerbated housing costs in the Bay Area, making the San Francisco metro among the cruelest markets in the U.S. Over the same period, Houston added 346,000 jobs and permitted 260,000 new dwellings, five times as many units per new job as San Francisco.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Why+Can%E2%80%99t+They+Build+More+Homes+Where+the+Jobs+Are%3F&amp;rft.date=2017-06-23&amp;rft.aulast=Clark&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrick&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bloomberg.com%2Fnews%2Farticles%2F2017-06-23%2Fwhy-can-t-they-build-more-homes-where-the-jobs-are&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASan+Francisco+Bay+Area">
